      <p>
       <b>
        Nicaragua
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
           <span title="'w' in 'wind'">
            w
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          , -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
          </span>
          -, -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
           <span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">
            j
           </span>
           <span title="/u/: 'u' in 'influence'">
            u
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Nicaragua.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/En-us-Nicaragua.ogg" title="En-us-Nicaragua.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ;
       <small>
        Spanish:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
         [nikaˈɾaɣwa]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Nicaragua
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rep%C3%BAblica_de_Nicaragua.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/be/Rep%C3%BAblica_de_Nicaragua.ogg" title="República de Nicaragua.ogg">
          <span class="unicode" lang="es">
           <i>
            República de Nicaragua
           </i>
          </span>
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rep%C3%BAblica_de_Nicaragua.ogg" title="File:República de Nicaragua.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ), is the largest country in the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central American
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus" title="Isthmus">
        isthmus
       </a>
       , bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       to the north, the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       to the east,
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       to the south, and the Pacific Ocean to the west.
       <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">
        Managua
       </a>
       is the country's capital and largest city and is also the third-largest city in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       , behind
       <a href="/wiki/Tegucigalpa" title="Tegucigalpa">
        Tegucigalpa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala_City" title="Guatemala City">
        Guatemala City
       </a>
       . The multi-ethnic population of six million includes people of indigenous, European, African, and Asian heritage. The main language is Spanish. Native tribes on the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       speak their own languages and English.
      </p>
      <p>
       Originally inhabited by various indigenous cultures since ancient times, the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       conquered the region in the 16th century. Nicaragua gained independence from Spain in 1821. The Mosquito Coast followed a different historical path, with the English colonizing it in the 17th century and later coming under the British rule, as well as some minor Spanish interludes in the 19th century. It became an autonomous territory of Nicaragua in 1860 and the northernmost part of it was later transferred to
       <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">
        Honduras
       </a>
       in 1960. Since its independence, Nicaragua has undergone periods of political unrest, dictatorship, and fiscal crisis—the most notable causes that led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">
        Nicaraguan Revolution
       </a>
       of the 1960s and 1970s and the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution#Contra_War" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">
        Contra War
       </a>
       of the 1980s. Nicaragua is a
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       republic.
      </p>
      <p>
       The mixture of cultural traditions has generated substantial diversity in folklore, cuisine, music, and literature, particularly the latter given the literary contributions of Nicaraguan poets and writers, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo" title="Rubén Darío">
        Rubén Darío
       </a>
       . Known as the "land of lakes and volcanoes",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brierley_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brierley-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wallace_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wallace-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua is also home to the second-largest rainforest of the Americas. The country has set a goal for itself to have 90% renewable energy by the year 2020.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The biological diversity, warm tropical climate and active volcanoes make Nicaragua an increasingly popular
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourist_destination" title="Tourist destination">
        tourist destination
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">

          <span class="tocnumber">

           Geography and climate
          </span>
         </a>

      <p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       There are two prevailing theories on how the name "Nicaragua" came about. The first is that the name was coined by Spanish colonists based on the name
       <a href="/wiki/Nicarao_(cacique)" title="Nicarao (cacique)">
        Nicarao
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ideal_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ideal-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who was the chieftain or
       <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">
        cacique
       </a>
       of a powerful indigenous tribe encountered by the Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">
        conquistador
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gil_Gonz%C3%A1lez_D%C3%A1vila" title="Gil González Dávila">
        Gil González Dávila
       </a>
       during his entry into southwestern Nicaragua in 1522. This theory holds that the name Nicaragua was formed as a
       <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">
        portmanteau
       </a>
       of Nicarao and the word
       <i>
        agua
       </i>
       which means "water" in Spanish, to reference the fact that there are two large lakes and several other bodies of water within the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pueblo_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pueblo-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, as of 2002, it was determined that the cacique's real name was Macuilmiquiztli, which meant "Five Deaths" in the
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       language, rather than Nicarao.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanchez_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sanchez-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encuentro_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encuentro-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The second theory is that the country's name comes from any of the following Nahuatl words:
       <i>
        nic-anahuac
       </i>
       , which meant "
       <a href="/wiki/Anahuac_(Aztec)" title="Anahuac (Aztec)">
        Anahuac
       </a>
       reached this far", or "the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuas" title="Nahuas">
        Nahuas
       </a>
       came this far", or "those who come from Anahuac came this far";
       <i>
        nican-nahua
       </i>
       , which meant "here are the Nahuas"; or
       <i>
        nic-atl-nahuac
       </i>
       , which meant "here by the water" or "surrounded by water".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ideal_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ideal-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pueblo_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pueblo-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Choque_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Choque-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nicaragua" title="History of Nicaragua">
        History of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-notice" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg">
           <img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" data-file-height="44" data-file-width="44" height="44" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" width="44"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This article
          <b>
           is missing information about
           <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
            Mosquito Coast
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please expand the article to include this information. Further details may exist on the
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:Nicaragua" title="Talk:Nicaragua">
            talk page
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (December 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_history">
        Pre-Columbian history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-Columbian history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg/220px-Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg/330px-Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg/440px-Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_Ometepe_p%C3%A9troglyphes_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An ancient
         <a href="/wiki/Petroglyph" title="Petroglyph">
          petroglyph
         </a>
         on
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ometepe_Island" title="Ometepe Island">
          Ometepe Island
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paleo-Americans" title="Paleo-Americans">
        Paleo-Americans
       </a>
       first inhabited what is now known as Nicaragua as far back as 12,000 BCE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dall2005_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dall2005-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In later
       <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">
        pre-Columbian
       </a>
       times, Nicaragua's
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        indigenous people
       </a>
       were part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_Area" title="Intermediate Area">
        Intermediate Area
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         33
        </span>
       </sup>
       between the
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
        Andean
       </a>
       cultural regions, and within the influence of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isthmo-Colombian" title="Isthmo-Colombian">
        Isthmo-Colombian
       </a>
       area. Nicaragua's central region and its Caribbean coast were inhabited by
       <a href="/wiki/Macro-Chibchan_languages" title="Macro-Chibchan languages">
        Macro-Chibchan language
       </a>
       ethnic groups.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         20
        </span>
       </sup>
       They had coalesced in Central America and migrated also to present-day northern Colombia and nearby areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They lived a life based primarily on hunting and gathering, as well as fishing, and performing
       <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">
        slash-and-burn
       </a>
       agriculture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         33
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         65
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the end of the 15th century, western Nicaragua was inhabited by several different indigenous peoples related by culture to the Mesoamerican civilizations of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">
        Aztec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_peoples" title="Maya peoples">
        Maya
       </a>
       , and by language to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoamerican_Linguistic_Area" title="Mesoamerican Linguistic Area">
        Mesoamerican Linguistic Area
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC1_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC1-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Chorotegas were
       <a href="/wiki/Mangue_language" title="Mangue language">
        Mangue language
       </a>
       ethnic groups who had arrived in Nicaragua from what is now the Mexican state of
       <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">
        Chiapas
       </a>
       sometime around 800 CE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Choque_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Choque-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         26–33
        </span>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_people" title="Pipil people">
        Pipil-Nicarao
       </a>
       people were a branch of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuas" title="Nahuas">
        Nahuas
       </a>
       who spoke the
       <a href="/wiki/Pipil_language" title="Pipil language">
        Nahuat
       </a>
       dialect, and like the Chorotegas, they too had come from Chiapas to Nicaragua in approximately 1200 CE.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Prior to that, the Pipil-Nicaraos had been associated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Toltec" title="Toltec">
        Toltec
       </a>
       civilization.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         26–33
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both the Chorotegas and the Pipil-Nicaraos were originally from Mexico's
       <a href="/wiki/Cholula_(Mesoamerican_site)" title="Cholula (Mesoamerican site)">
        Cholula
       </a>
       valley,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell1985_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Campbell1985-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and had gradually migrated southward.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         26–33
        </span>
       </sup>
       Additionally, there were trade-related colonies in Nicaragua that had been set up by the Aztecs starting in the 14th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         26–33
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spanish_era_.281522.E2.80.931821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_era_(1522–1821)">
        Spanish era (1522–1821)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spanish era (1522–1821)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish colonization of the Americas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_Nicaragua" title="Spanish conquest of Nicaragua">
        Spanish conquest of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2328" data-file-width="3210" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG/220px-06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG/330px-06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG/440px-06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:06.Plaza_de_la_Independencia_de_Granada.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Colonial
         <a href="/wiki/Granada,_Nicaragua" title="Granada, Nicaragua">
          City of Granada
         </a>
         near
         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nicaragua" title="Lake Nicaragua">
          Lake Nicaragua
         </a>
         is one of the most visited sites in
         <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
          Central America
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1502, on his fourth voyage,
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       became the first European known to have reached what is now Nicaragua as he sailed southeast toward the
       <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">
        Isthmus of Panama
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         193
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         92
        </span>
       </sup>
       Columbus explored the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       on the Atlantic side of Nicaragua
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but did not encounter any indigenous people. 20 years later, the Spaniards returned to Nicaragua, this time to its southwestern part. The first attempt to conquer Nicaragua was by the conquistador
       <a href="/wiki/Gil_Gonz%C3%A1lez_D%C3%A1vila" title="Gil González Dávila">
        Gil González Dávila
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBH_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EBH-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who had arrived in Panama in January 1520. In 1522, González Dávila ventured into the area that later became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Rivas_Department" title="Rivas Department">
        Rivas Department
       </a>
       of Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         35
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         92
        </span>
       </sup>
       It was there that he encountered an indigenous Nahua tribe led by a chieftain named Macuilmiquiztli, whose name has sometimes been erroneously referred to as "
       <a href="/wiki/Nicarao_(cacique)" title="Nicarao (cacique)">
        Nicarao
       </a>
       " or "Nicaragua". At the time, the tribe's capital city was called Quauhcapolca.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encuentro_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encuentro-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HealyPohl1980_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HealyPohl1980-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dyck2015_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dyck2015-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       González Dávila had brought along two indigenous interpreters who had been taught the Spanish language, and thus he was able to have a discourse with Macuilmiquiztli.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanchez_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Sanchez-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After exploring and gathering gold
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encuentro_18-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encuentro-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         35
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         55
        </span>
       </sup>
       in the fertile western valleys, González Dávila and his men were attacked and driven off by Chorotega natives led by the chieftain
       <a href="/wiki/Diriangen" title="Diriangen">
        Diriangen
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encuentro_18-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encuentro-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Spanish attempted to convert the tribes to Christianity; the people in Macuilmiquiztli's tribe were baptized,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encuentro_18-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Encuentro-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         86
        </span>
       </sup>
       but Diriangen, however, was openly hostile to the Spaniards.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first Spanish permanent settlements were founded in 1524.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBH_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-EBH-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       That year, the conquistador
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Hern%C3%A1ndez_de_C%C3%B3rdoba_(founder_of_Nicaragua)" title="Francisco Hernández de Córdoba (founder of Nicaragua)">
        Francisco Hernández de Córdoba
       </a>
       founded two of Nicaragua's principal cities:
       <a href="/wiki/Granada,_Nicaragua" title="Granada, Nicaragua">
        Granada
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nicaragua" title="Lake Nicaragua">
        Lake Nicaragua
       </a>
       was the first settlement, followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Nicaragua" title="León, Nicaragua">
        León
       </a>
       at a location west of
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Managua" title="Lake Managua">
        Lake Managua
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         35, 193
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         92
        </span>
       </sup>
       Córdoba soon built defenses for the cities and fought against incursions by other conquistadors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         92
        </span>
       </sup>
       Córdoba was later publicly
       <a href="/wiki/Decapitation" title="Decapitation">
        beheaded
       </a>
       as a consequence for having defied the authority of his superior,
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Arias_D%C3%A1vila" title="Pedro Arias Dávila">
        Pedro Arias Dávila
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         35
        </span>
       </sup>
       Córdoba's tomb and remains were discovered in 2000 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_Viejo" title="León Viejo">
        ruins of León Viejo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ET-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The clashes among Spanish forces did not impede their destruction of the indigenous people and their culture. The series of battles came to be known as the "War of the Captains".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Pedro Arias Dávila was a winner;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         35
        </span>
       </sup>
       although he had lost control of Panama, he moved to Nicaragua and successfully established his base in León.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whisnant2000_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Whisnant2000-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1527, León became the capital of the colony.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         93
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whisnant2000_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Whisnant2000-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Through adroit diplomatic machinations, Arias Dávila became the colony's first governor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET_36-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ET-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Without women in their parties,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         123
        </span>
       </sup>
       the Spanish conquerors took Nahua and Chorotega wives and partners, beginning the multiethnic mix of native and European stock now known as "
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
         mestizo
        </a>
       </i>
       ", which constitutes the great majority of the population in western Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC1_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOC1-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many indigenous people died as a result of new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">
        infectious diseases
       </a>
       , compounded by neglect by the Spaniards, who controlled their subsistence.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBH_32-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-EBH-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Furthermore, a large number of other natives were captured and transported to Panama and Peru between 1526 and 1540, where they were forced to perform slave labor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         193
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newson_25-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newson-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         104–105
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1610, the
       <a href="/wiki/Momotombo" title="Momotombo">
        Momotombo
       </a>
       volcano erupted, destroying the city of León.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geomorph_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geomorph-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city was rebuilt northwest of the original,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whisnant2000_38-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Whisnant2000-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geomorph_39-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geomorph-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which is now known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_Viejo" title="León Viejo">
        ruins of León Viejo
       </a>
       . During the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">
        American Revolutionary War
       </a>
       , Central America was subject to conflict between Britain and Spain. British navy admiral
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson">
        Horatio Nelson
       </a>
       led expeditions in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Fernando_de_Omoa" title="Battle of San Fernando de Omoa">
        Battle of San Fernando de Omoa
       </a>
       in 1779 and on the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Expedition_(1780)" title="San Juan Expedition (1780)">
        San Juan River in 1780
       </a>
       , the latter of which had temporary success before being abandoned due to disease.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_.281821.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1821)">
        Independence (1821)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Independence (1821)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png/220px-Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png/330px-Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png/440px-Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1830_na.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">
          Federal Republic of Central America
         </a>
         and British colony of the
         <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
          Mosquito Coast
         </a>
         in 1830
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Captaincy_General_of_Guatemala" title="Captaincy General of Guatemala">
        Captaincy General of Guatemala
       </a>
       was dissolved in September 1821 with the
       <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Independence_of_Central_America" title="Act of Independence of Central America">
        Act of Independence of Central America
       </a>
       , and Nicaragua soon became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Mexican_Empire" title="First Mexican Empire">
        First Mexican Empire
       </a>
       . After the monarchy of the First Mexican Empire was overthrown in 1823, Nicaragua joined the newly formed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_Central_America" title="United Provinces of Central America">
        United Provinces of Central America
       </a>
       , which was later renamed as the
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Central_America" title="Federal Republic of Central America">
        Federal Republic of Central America
       </a>
       . Nicaragua finally became an independent republic in 1838.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rivalry between the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutionalist_Liberal_Party_(Nicaragua)" title="Constitutionalist Liberal Party (Nicaragua)">
        Liberal
       </a>
       elite of León and the
       <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(Nicaragua)" title="Conservative Party (Nicaragua)">
        Conservative
       </a>
       elite of Granada characterized the early years of independence and often degenerated into civil war, particularly during the 1840s and 1850s.
       <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">
        Managua
       </a>
       was chosen as the nation's capital in 1852 to allay the rivalry between the two feuding cities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Capital_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Capital-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the days of the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">
        California Gold Rush
       </a>
       , Nicaragua provided a route for travelers from the eastern United States to journey to California by sea, via the use of the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_River_(Nicaragua)" title="San Juan River (Nicaragua)">
        San Juan River
       </a>
       and Lake Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         81
        </span>
       </sup>
       Invited by the Liberals in 1855 to join their struggle against the Conservatives, a United States adventurer and
       <a href="/wiki/Filibuster_(military)" title="Filibuster (military)">
        filibuster
       </a>
       named
       <a href="/wiki/William_Walker_(filibuster)" title="William Walker (filibuster)">
        William Walker
       </a>
       set himself up as President of Nicaragua, after conducting a farcical election in 1856. Costa Rica, Honduras, and other Central American countries united to drive Walker out of Nicaragua in 1857,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       after which a period of three decades of Conservative rule ensued.
      </p>
      <p>
       Great Britain, which had claimed the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">
        protectorate
       </a>
       since 1655, delegated the area to Honduras in 1859 before transferring it to Nicaragua in 1860. The Mosquito Coast remained an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">
        autonomous area
       </a>
       until 1894.
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Santos_Zelaya" title="José Santos Zelaya">
        José Santos Zelaya
       </a>
       , President of Nicaragua from 1893 to 1909, negotiated the annexation of the Mosquito Coast to the rest of Nicaragua. In his honor, the region was named "
       <a href="/wiki/Zelaya_Department" title="Zelaya Department">
        Zelaya Department
       </a>
       ".
      </p>
      <p>
       Throughout the late 19th century, the United States and several European powers considered a scheme to build a
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua_Canal" title="Nicaragua Canal">
        canal across Nicaragua
       </a>
       , linking the Pacific Ocean to the Atlantic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="United_States_intervention_.281909.E2.80.9333.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_intervention_(1909–33)">
        United States intervention (1909–33)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: United States intervention (1909–33)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Nicaragua" title="United States occupation of Nicaragua">
        United States occupation of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1909, the United States provided political support to Conservative-led forces rebelling against President Zelaya. On November 18, 1909, U.S. warships were sent to the area after 500 revolutionaries (including two Americans) were executed by order of Zelaya. Zelaya resigned later that year.
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 1912, the President of Nicaragua,
       <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_D%C3%ADaz" title="Adolfo Díaz">
        Adolfo Díaz
       </a>
       , requested the secretary of war, General
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mena" title="Luis Mena">
        Luis Mena
       </a>
       , to resign for fear he was leading an insurrection. Mena fled Managua with his brother, the chief of police of Managua, to start an insurrection. When the U.S. delegation asked President Díaz to ensure the safety of American citizens and property during the insurrection, he replied he could not, and asked the United States to intervene in the conflict.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">
        United States Marines
       </a>
       occupied Nicaragua from 1912 to 1933,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         111, 197
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       except for a nine-month period beginning in 1925. In 1914, the
       <a href="/wiki/Bryan%E2%80%93Chamorro_Treaty" title="Bryan–Chamorro Treaty">
        Bryan–Chamorro Treaty
       </a>
       was signed, giving the U.S. control over a proposed canal through Nicaragua, as well as leases for potential canal defenses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following the evacuation of U.S. Marines, another
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_civil_war_(1926%E2%80%9327)" title="Nicaraguan civil war (1926–27)">
        violent conflict
       </a>
       between Liberals and Conservatives took place in 1926, which resulted in the return of U.S. Marines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:General_Sandino_(center)_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.,_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1869" data-file-width="3000" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/General_Sandino_%28center%29_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.%2C_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif/lossy-page1-220px-General_Sandino_%28center%29_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.%2C_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/General_Sandino_%28center%29_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.%2C_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif/lossy-page1-330px-General_Sandino_%28center%29_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.%2C_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/General_Sandino_%28center%29_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.%2C_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif/lossy-page1-440px-General_Sandino_%28center%29_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.%2C_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:General_Sandino_(center)_and_Staff_enroute_to_Mexico._Siglo_XX.,_06-1929_-_NARA_-_532357.tif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rebel leader
         <a href="/wiki/Augusto_C%C3%A9sar_Sandino" title="Augusto César Sandino">
          Augusto César Sandino
         </a>
         (center)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       From 1927 until 1933, rebel general
       <a href="/wiki/Augusto_C%C3%A9sar_Sandino" title="Augusto César Sandino">
        Augusto César Sandino
       </a>
       led a sustained guerrilla war first against the Conservative regime and subsequently against the U.S. Marines, whom he fought for over five years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When the Americans left in 1933, they set up the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_(Nicaragua)" title="National Guard (Nicaragua)">
         Guardia Nacional
        </a>
       </i>
       (national guard),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SY_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SY-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a combined military and police force trained and equipped by the Americans and designed to be loyal to U.S. interests.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the U.S. Marines withdrew from Nicaragua in January 1933, Sandino and the newly elected administration of President
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Sacasa" title="Juan Bautista Sacasa">
        Juan Bautista Sacasa
       </a>
       reached an agreement by which Sandino would cease his guerrilla activities in return for amnesty, a grant of land for an agricultural colony, and retention of an armed band of 100 men for a year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, due to a growing hostility between Sandino and National Guard director
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasio_Somoza_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Anastasio Somoza García">
        Anastasio Somoza García
       </a>
       and a fear of armed opposition from Sandino, Somoza García decided to order his assassination.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SY_52-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-SY-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Sandino was invited by Sacasa to have dinner and sign a peace treaty at the Presidential House in Managua on the night of February 21, 1934. After leaving the Presidential House, Sandino's car was stopped by soldiers of the National Guard and they kidnapped him. Later that night, Sandino was assassinated by soldiers of the National Guard. Hundreds of men, women, and children from Sandino's agricultural colony were executed later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SomozaDynasty_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SomozaDynasty-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Somoza_dynasty_.281927.E2.80.931979.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Somoza_dynasty_(1927–1979)">
        Somoza dynasty (1927–1979)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Somoza dynasty (1927–1979)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="570" data-file-width="617" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg/220px-Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg/330px-Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg/440px-Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trujillo-Somoza_1952.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         President
         <a href="/wiki/Anastasio_Somoza_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Anastasio Somoza García">
          Anastasio Somoza García
         </a>
         (left), with
         <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
          Dominican
         </a>
         President
         <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">
          Rafael Trujillo
         </a>
         , 1952
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua has experienced several military dictatorships, the longest being the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hereditary_dictatorship" title="Hereditary dictatorship">
        hereditary dictatorship
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Somoza_family" title="Somoza family">
        Somoza family
       </a>
       , who ruled for 43 nonconsecutive years during the 20th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Somoza family came to power as part of a U.S.-engineered pact in 1927 that stipulated the formation of the
       <i>
        Guardia Nacional
       </i>
       to replace the marines who had long reigned in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Somoza García slowly eliminated officers in the national guard who might have stood in his way, and then deposed Sacasa and became president on January 1, 1937, in a
       <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">
        rigged election
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SY_52-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-SY-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua declared war on Germany on December 8, 1941, during World War II.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       No soldiers were sent to the war, but Somoza García did seize the occasion to confiscate properties held by
       <a href="/wiki/German_Nicaraguan" title="German Nicaraguan">
        German Nicaraguan
       </a>
       residents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1945, Nicaragua was among the first countries to ratify the United Nations Charter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua,_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="1152" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua%2C_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg/220px-Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua%2C_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua%2C_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg/330px-Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua%2C_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua%2C_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg/440px-Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua%2C_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meeting_with_President_Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle_of_Nicaragua,_before_State_Dinner_-_NARA_-_194723-perspective-tilt-crop.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle" title="Anastasio Somoza Debayle">
          Anastasio Somoza Debayle
         </a>
         (center) with
         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
          Richard Nixon
         </a>
         , 1971
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On September 21, 1956, Somoza García was shot to death by
       <a href="/wiki/Rigoberto_L%C3%B3pez_P%C3%A9rez" title="Rigoberto López Pérez">
        Rigoberto López Pérez
       </a>
       , a 27-year-old Liberal Nicaraguan poet.
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Somoza_Debayle" title="Luis Somoza Debayle">
        Luis Somoza Debayle
       </a>
       , the eldest son of the late president, was appointed president by the congress and officially took charge of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SY_52-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-SY-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He is remembered by some for being moderate, but was in power only for a few years and then died of a heart attack. His successor as president was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Schick_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="René Schick Gutiérrez">
        René Schick Gutiérrez
       </a>
       , whom most Nicaraguans viewed "as nothing more than a puppet of the Somozas".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Somoza García's youngest son,
       <a href="/wiki/Anastasio_Somoza_Debayle" title="Anastasio Somoza Debayle">
        Anastasio Somoza Debayle
       </a>
       , often referred to simply as "Somoza", became president in 1967.
      </p>
      <p>
       An
       <a href="/wiki/1972_Nicaragua_earthquake" title="1972 Nicaragua earthquake">
        earthquake in 1972
       </a>
       destroyed nearly 90% of Managua, creating major losses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Instead of helping to rebuild Managua, Somoza siphoned off relief money. The mishandling of relief money also prompted
       <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">
        Pittsburgh Pirates
       </a>
       star
       <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Clemente" title="Roberto Clemente">
        Roberto Clemente
       </a>
       to personally fly to Managua on December 31, 1972, but he died
       <i>
        en route
       </i>
       in an airplane accident.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even the economic elite were reluctant to support Somoza, as he had acquired monopolies in industries that were key to rebuilding the nation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Somoza family was among a few families or groups of influential firms which reaped most of the benefits of the country's growth from the 1950s to the 1970s. When Somoza was deposed by the Sandinistas in 1979, the family's worth was estimated to be between $500 million and $1.5 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Nicaraguan_Revolution_.281960s.E2.80.931990.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nicaraguan_Revolution_(1960s–1990)">
        Nicaraguan Revolution (1960s–1990)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Nicaraguan Revolution (1960s–1990)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">
        Nicaraguan Revolution
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="792" data-file-width="1160" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg/220px-Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg/330px-Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg/440px-Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smoke_break_el_serrano_1987.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         United States–supported anti-Sandinista "
         <a href="/wiki/Contras" title="Contras">
          Contra
         </a>
         " rebels (ARDE Frente Sur) in 1987.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1961,
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fonseca" title="Carlos Fonseca">
        Carlos Fonseca
       </a>
       looked back to the historical figure of Sandino, and along with two other people (one of whom was believed to be Casimiro Sotelo, who was later assassinated), founded the
       <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">
        Sandinista National Liberation Front
       </a>
       (FSLN).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SY_52-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-SY-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the 1972 earthquake and Somoza's apparent corruption, the ranks of the Sandinistas were flooded with young disaffected Nicaraguans who no longer had anything to lose.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grinnell2007_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Grinnell2007-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 1974, a group of the FSLN, in an attempt to kidnap U.S. ambassador Turner Shelton, held some Managuan partygoers hostage (after killing the host, former agriculture minister, Jose Maria Castillo), until the Somozan government met their demands for a large ransom and free transport to Cuba. Somoza granted this, then subsequently sent his national guard out into the countryside to look for the perpetrators of the kidnapping, described by opponents of the kidnapping as "terrorists".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On January 10, 1978,
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Joaqu%C3%ADn_Chamorro_Cardenal" title="Pedro Joaquín Chamorro Cardenal">
        Pedro Joaquín Chamorro Cardenal
       </a>
       , the editor of the national newspaper
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Prensa_(Managua)" title="La Prensa (Managua)">
         La Prensa
        </a>
       </i>
       and ardent opponent of Somoza, was assassinated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AC_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AC-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is alleged that the planners and perpetrators of the murder were at the highest echelons of the Somoza regime.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AC_69-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AC-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Sandinistas forcefully took power in July 1979, ousting Somoza, and prompting the exodus of the majority of Nicaragua's middle class, wealthy landowners, and professionals, many of whom settled in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Carter administration decided to work with the new government, while attaching a provision for aid forfeiture if it was found to be assisting insurgencies in neighboring countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Somoza fled the country and eventually ended up in
       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">
        Paraguay
       </a>
       , where he was assassinated in September 1980, allegedly by members of the Argentinian Revolutionary Workers' Party.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1980, the Carter administration provided $60 million in aid to Nicaragua under the Sandinistas, but the aid was suspended when the administration obtained evidence of Nicaraguan shipment of arms to El Salvadoran rebels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response to the coming to power of the Sandinistas, various rebel groups collectively known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Contras" title="Contras">
        contras
       </a>
       " were formed to oppose the new government. The
       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">
        Reagan
       </a>
       administration authorized the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">
        CIA
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_and_state-sponsored_terrorism" title="United States and state-sponsored terrorism">
        help the contra rebels
       </a>
       with funding, armaments, and training.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CA_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CA-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The contras operated out of camps in the neighboring countries of Honduras to the north and Costa Rica to the south.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CA_76-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CA-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua,_1989.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="421" data-file-width="600" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua%2C_1989.jpg/220px-10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua%2C_1989.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua%2C_1989.jpg/330px-10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua%2C_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua%2C_1989.jpg/440px-10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua%2C_1989.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:10th_anniversary_of_the_Nicaraguan_revolution_in_Managua,_1989.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         10th anniversary of the Nicaraguan revolution in Managua, 1989
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       They engaged in a systematic campaign of terror amongst the rural Nicaraguan population to disrupt the social reform projects of the Sandinistas. Several historians have criticized the contra campaign and the
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_Ronald_Reagan_administration" title="Foreign policy of the Ronald Reagan administration">
        Reagan administration's support for it
       </a>
       , citing the brutality and numerous human rights violations of the contras. LaRamee and Polakoff, for example, describe the destruction of health centers, schools, and cooperatives at the hands of the rebels,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and others have contended that murder, rape, and torture occurred on a large scale in contra-dominated areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The United States also carried out a campaign of economic sabotage, and disrupted shipping by planting underwater mines in Nicaragua's port of
       <a href="/wiki/Corinto,_Nicaragua" title="Corinto, Nicaragua">
        Corinto
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       an action condemned by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
        International Court of Justice
       </a>
       as illegal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The U.S. also sought to place economic pressure on the Sandinistas, and the Reagan administration imposed a full trade embargo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Sandinistas were also accused of human rights abuses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_general_election,_1984" title="Nicaraguan general election, 1984">
        Nicaraguan general elections of 1984
       </a>
       , which were judged to have been free and fair, the Sandinistas won the parliamentary election and their leader
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ortega" title="Daniel Ortega">
        Daniel Ortega
       </a>
       won the presidential election.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Reagan administration criticized the elections as a "sham" based on the charge that
       <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Cruz" title="Arturo Cruz">
        Arturo Cruz
       </a>
       , the candidate nominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Coordinadora_Democr%C3%A1tica_Nicarag%C3%BCense" title="Coordinadora Democrática Nicaragüense">
        Coordinadora Democrática Nicaragüense
       </a>
       , comprising three right wing political parties, did not participate in the elections. However, the administration privately argued against Cruz's participation for fear his involvement would legitimize the elections, and thus weaken the case for American aid to the contras.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to Martin Kriele, the results of the election were rigged.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the U.S. Congress prohibited federal funding of the contras in 1983, the Reagan administration nonetheless illegally continued to back them by covertly selling arms to
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       and channeling the proceeds to the contras (the
       <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Contra_affair" title="Iran–Contra affair">
        Iran–Contra affair
       </a>
       ), for which several members of the Reagan administration were convicted of felonies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
        International Court of Justice
       </a>
       , in regard to the case of
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua_v._United_States" title="Nicaragua v. United States">
        Nicaragua v. United States
       </a>
       in 1984, found, "the United States of America was under an obligation to make reparation to the Republic of Nicaragua for all injury caused to Nicaragua by certain breaches of obligations under customary international law and treaty-law committed by the United States of America".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the war between the contras and the Sandinistas, 30,000 people were killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Post-war_.281990.E2.80.93present.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_(1990–present)">
        Post-war (1990–present)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Post-war (1990–present)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Violeta_Chamorro_1993.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="253" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Violeta_Chamorro_1993.jpg/170px-Violeta_Chamorro_1993.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Violeta_Chamorro_1993.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Violeta_Chamorro_1993.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Violeta_Chamorro" title="Violeta Chamorro">
          Violeta Chamorro
         </a>
         in 1990 became the first woman president democratically elected in the Americas.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_general_election,_1990" title="Nicaraguan general election, 1990">
        Nicaraguan general election, 1990
       </a>
       , a coalition of anti-Sandinista parties (from the left and right of the political spectrum) led by
       <a href="/wiki/Violeta_Chamorro" title="Violeta Chamorro">
        Violeta Chamorro
       </a>
       , the widow of Pedro Joaquín Chamorro Cardenal, defeated the Sandinistas. The defeat shocked the Sandinistas, who had expected to win.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Commentators such as
       <a href="/wiki/Noam_Chomsky" title="Noam Chomsky">
        Noam Chomsky
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Brian_Willson" title="Brian Willson">
