        Brian Willson
       </a>
       attributed the outcome to the U.S.-Contra threats to continue the war if the Sandinistas retained power, the general
       <a href="/wiki/War-weariness" title="War-weariness">
        war-weariness
       </a>
       of the Nicaraguan population, and the abysmal Nicaraguan economic situation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Exit polls of Nicaraguans reported Chamorro's victory over Ortega was achieved with a 55% majority.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chamorro was the first woman president of Nicaragua. Ortega vowed he would govern
       <i>
        desde abajo
       </i>
       (from below).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chamorro came to office with an economy in ruins, primarily because of the financial and social costs of the contra war with the Sandinista-led government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the next election, the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_general_election,_1996" title="Nicaraguan general election, 1996">
        Nicaraguan general election, 1996
       </a>
       , Daniel Ortega and the Sandinistas of the FSLN were defeated again, this time by
       <a href="/wiki/Arnoldo_Alem%C3%A1n" title="Arnoldo Alemán">
        Arnoldo Alemán
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutionalist_Liberal_Party_(Nicaragua)" title="Constitutionalist Liberal Party (Nicaragua)">
        Constitutional Liberal Party
       </a>
       (PLC).
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mitch-Flooding_in_Managua.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="168" data-file-width="250" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Mitch-Flooding_in_Managua.jpg/220px-Mitch-Flooding_in_Managua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/Mitch-Flooding_in_Managua.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mitch-Flooding_in_Managua.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Flooding in Lake Managua after the
         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">
          Hurricane Mitch
         </a>
         in 1998
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_general_election,_2001" title="Nicaraguan general election, 2001">
        the 2001 elections
       </a>
       , the PLC again defeated the FSLN, with Alemán's Vice President
       <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Bola%C3%B1os" title="Enrique Bolaños">
        Enrique Bolaños
       </a>
       succeeding him as President. Subsequently, however, Alemán was convicted and sentenced in 2003 to 20 years in prison for
       <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">
        embezzlement
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">
        money laundering
       </a>
       , and corruption;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       liberal and Sandinista parliament members subsequently combined to strip the presidential powers of President Bolaños and his ministers, calling for his resignation and threatening
       <a href="/wiki/Impeachment" title="Impeachment">
        impeachment
       </a>
       . The Sandinistas said they no longer supported Bolaños after U.S. Secretary of State
       <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">
        Colin Powell
       </a>
       told Bolaños to keep his distance from the FSLN.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This "slow motion
       <i>
        coup d'état
       </i>
       " was averted partially by pressure from the Central American presidents, who vowed not to recognize any movement that removed Bolaños; the U.S., the OAS, and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       also opposed the action.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Before
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_general_election,_2006" title="Nicaraguan general election, 2006">
        the general elections on November 5, 2006
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Nicaragua" title="National Assembly of Nicaragua">
        National Assembly
       </a>
       passed a bill further restricting
       <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Nicaragua" title="Abortion in Nicaragua">
        abortion in Nicaragua
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result, Nicaragua is one of five countries in the world where abortion is illegal with no exceptions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Legislative and presidential elections took place on November 5, 2006. Ortega returned to the presidency with 37.99% of the vote. This percentage was enough to win the presidency outright, because of a change in electoral law which lowered the percentage requiring a runoff election from 45% to 35% (with a 5% margin of victory).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua's 2011 general election resulted in re-election of Ortega, with a landslide victory and 62.46% of the vote. In 2014 the National Assembly approved changes to the constitution allowing Ortega to run for a third successive term.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In November 2016,
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_general_election,_2016" title="Nicaraguan general election, 2016">
        Ortega was elected for his third consecutive term
       </a>
       (his fourth overall). International monitoring of the elections was initially prohibited, and as a result the validity of the
       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Nicaragua" title="Elections in Nicaragua">
        elections
       </a>
       has been disputed, but observation by the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        OAS
       </a>
       was announced in October.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ortega was reported by Nicaraguan election officials as having received 72% of the vote. However the
       <a href="/wiki/Broad_Front_for_Democracy" title="Broad Front for Democracy">
        Broad Front for Democracy
       </a>
       (FAD), having promoted boycotts of the elections, claimed that 70% of voters had abstained (while election officials claimed 65.8% participation)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . Despite growing fears of
       <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">
        autocracy
       </a>
       and the increasing governmental powers of Ortega's wife
       <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Murillo" title="Rosario Murillo">
        Rosario Murillo
       </a>
       (m.1979)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as his vice president, Ortega is still popular among many Nicaraguans. This is largely due to the fact that under his presidency, gang violence has diminished,
       <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">
        poverty
       </a>
       levels have fallen, and Nicaraguan economic growth has surpassed other
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_economy" title="Latin American economy">
        Latin America
       </a>
       n countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">
        Geography and climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Nicaragua" title="Geography of Nicaragua">
        Geography of Nicaragua
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Nicaragua" title="Climate of Nicaragua">
        Climate of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volcanoes_of_Nicaragua" title="Volcanoes of Nicaragua">
        Volcanoes of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nicaragua map of Köppen climate classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua occupies a landmass of 130,967 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (50,567 sq mi). Nicaragua has three distinct geographical regions: the Pacific lowlands – fertile valleys which the Spanish colonists settled, the
       <a href="/wiki/Amerrisque_Mountains" title="Amerrisque Mountains">
        Amerrisque Mountains
       </a>
       (North-central highlands), and the Mosquito Coast (Atlantic lowlands/
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Lowlands" title="Caribbean Lowlands">
        Caribbean lowlands
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The low plains of the Atlantic Coast are 97 km (60 mi) wide in areas. They have long been exploited for their natural resources.
      </p>
      <p>
       On the Pacific side of Nicaragua are the two largest fresh water lakes in Central America—
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Managua" title="Lake Managua">
        Lake Managua
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nicaragua" title="Lake Nicaragua">
        Lake Nicaragua
       </a>
       . Surrounding these lakes and extending to their northwest along the
       <a href="/wiki/Rift_valley" title="Rift valley">
        rift valley
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">
        Gulf of Fonseca
       </a>
       are fertile lowland plains, with soil highly enriched by
       <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">
        ash
       </a>
       from nearby
       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">
        volcanoes
       </a>
       of the central highlands. Nicaragua's abundance of biologically significant and unique
       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">
        ecosystems
       </a>
       contribute to
       <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">
        Mesoamerica
       </a>
       's designation as a
       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">
        biodiversity hotspot
       </a>
       . Nicaragua has made efforts to become less dependent on fossil fuels, and it expects to acquire 90% of its energy from renewable resources by the year 2020.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nearly one fifth of Nicaragua is designated as
       <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Nicaragua" title="Protected areas of Nicaragua">
        protected areas
       </a>
       like national parks, nature reserves, and biological reserves.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geophysical" title="Geophysical">
        Geophysically
       </a>
       , Nicaragua is surrounded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">
        Caribbean Plate
       </a>
       , an
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">
        oceanic
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">
        tectonic plate
       </a>
       underlying Central America and the
       <a href="/wiki/Cocos_Plate" title="Cocos Plate">
        Cocos Plate
       </a>
       . Since Central America is a major
       <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">
        subduction
       </a>
       zone, Nicaragua hosts most of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Volcanic_Arc" title="Central American Volcanic Arc">
        Central American Volcanic Arc
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_lowlands">
        Pacific lowlands
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Pacific lowlands">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_(landscape).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_%28landscape%29.jpg/220px-Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_%28landscape%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_%28landscape%29.jpg/330px-Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_%28landscape%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_%28landscape%29.jpg/440px-Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_%28landscape%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concepci%C3%B3n_from_Maderas_(landscape).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nicaragua is known as the land of lakes and volcanoes; pictured is
         <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_(volcano)" title="Concepción (volcano)">
          Concepción volcano
         </a>
         , as seen from
         <a href="/wiki/Maderas" title="Maderas">
          Maderas volcano
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the west of the country, these lowlands consist of a broad, hot, fertile plain. Punctuating this plain are several large volcanoes of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cordillera_Los_Maribios" title="Cordillera Los Maribios">
        Cordillera Los Maribios
       </a>
       mountain range, including
       <a href="/wiki/Mombacho" title="Mombacho">
        Mombacho
       </a>
       just outside Granada, and
       <a href="/wiki/Momotombo" title="Momotombo">
        Momotombo
       </a>
       near León. The lowland area runs from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Fonseca" title="Gulf of Fonseca">
        Gulf of Fonseca
       </a>
       to Nicaragua's Pacific border with Costa Rica south of
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nicaragua" title="Lake Nicaragua">
        Lake Nicaragua
       </a>
       . Lake Nicaragua is the largest freshwater lake in Central America (20th largest in the world),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is home to some of the world's rare freshwater sharks (
       <a href="/wiki/Bull_shark" title="Bull shark">
        Nicaraguan shark
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Pacific lowlands region is the most populous, with over half of the nation's population.
      </p>
      <p>
       The eruptions of western Nicaragua's 40 volcanoes, many of which are still active, have sometimes devastated settlements but also have enriched the land with layers of fertile ash. The geologic activity that produces vulcanism also breeds powerful earthquakes. Tremors occur regularly throughout the Pacific zone, and earthquakes have nearly destroyed the capital city, Managua, more than once.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PenasBlancas,_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve,_Jinotega_Department,_Nicaragua.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/PenasBlancas%2C_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve%2C_Jinotega_Department%2C_Nicaragua.jpg/220px-PenasBlancas%2C_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve%2C_Jinotega_Department%2C_Nicaragua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/PenasBlancas%2C_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve%2C_Jinotega_Department%2C_Nicaragua.jpg/330px-PenasBlancas%2C_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve%2C_Jinotega_Department%2C_Nicaragua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/PenasBlancas%2C_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve%2C_Jinotega_Department%2C_Nicaragua.jpg/440px-PenasBlancas%2C_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve%2C_Jinotega_Department%2C_Nicaragua.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PenasBlancas,_part_of_the_Bosawas_Reserve,_Jinotega_Department,_Nicaragua.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Peñas Blancas, part of the
         <a href="/wiki/Bosaw%C3%A1s_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Bosawás Biosphere Reserve">
          Bosawás Biosphere Reserve
         </a>
         is the second largest rainforest in the Western Hemisphere, after the Amazonian Rainforest in Brazil. Located northeast of the city of
         <a href="/wiki/Jinotega" title="Jinotega">
          Jinotega
         </a>
         in Northeastern Nicaragua.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most of the Pacific zone is
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tierra_caliente" title="Tierra caliente">
         tierra caliente
        </a>
       </i>
       , the "hot land" of tropical Spanish America at elevations under 610 metres (2,000 ft). Temperatures remain virtually constant throughout the year, with highs ranging between 29.4 and 32.2 °C (85 and 90 °F). After a dry season lasting from November to April, rains begin in May and continue to October, giving the Pacific lowlands 1,016 to 1,524 millimetres (40 to 60 in) of precipitation. Good soils and a favourable climate combine to make western Nicaragua the country's economic and demographic centre. The southwestern shore of Lake Nicaragua lies within 24 kilometres (15 mi) of the Pacific Ocean. Thus the lake and the San Juan River were often proposed in the 19th century as the longest part of a canal route across the Central American isthmus. Canal proposals were periodically revived in the 20th and 21st centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Roughly a century after the opening of the
       <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">
        Panama Canal
       </a>
       , the prospect of a Nicaraguan
       <a href="/wiki/Ecocanal" title="Ecocanal">
        ecocanal
       </a>
       remains a topic of interest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to its beach and resort communities, the Pacific lowlands contains most of Nicaragua's Spanish colonial architecture and artifacts. Cities such as León and
       <a href="/wiki/Granada,_Nicaragua" title="Granada, Nicaragua">
        Granada
       </a>
       abound in colonial architecture; founded in 1524, Granada is the oldest colonial city in the Americas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="North_central_highlands">
        North central highlands
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: North central highlands">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG/220px-Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG/330px-Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG/440px-Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ca%C3%B1onsomoto.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Somoto_Canyon_National_Monument" title="Somoto Canyon National Monument">
          Somoto Canyon National Monument
         </a>
         is located in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somoto" title="Somoto">
          Somoto
         </a>
         in the
         <a href="/wiki/Madriz_Department" title="Madriz Department">
          Madriz Department
         </a>
         in Northern Nicaragua.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Northern Nicaragua is the most diversified region producing coffee, cattle, milk products, vegetables, wood, gold, and flowers. Its extensive forests, rivers and geography are suited for ecotourism.
      </p>
      <p>
       The central highlands are a significantly less populated and economically developed area in the north, between Lake Nicaragua and the Caribbean. Forming the country's
       <a href="/wiki/Tierra_templada" title="Tierra templada">
        tierra templada
       </a>
       , or "temperate land", at elevations between 610 and 1,524 metres (2,000 and 5,000 ft), the highlands enjoy mild temperatures with daily highs of 23.9 to 26.7 °C (75 to 80 °F). This region has a longer, wetter rainy season than the Pacific lowlands, making erosion a problem on its steep slopes. Rugged terrain, poor soils, and low population density characterize the area as a whole, but the northwestern valleys are fertile and well settled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The area has a cooler climate than the Pacific lowlands. About a quarter of the country's agriculture takes place in this region, with coffee grown on the higher slopes.
       <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">
        Oaks
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">
        pines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">
        moss
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">
        ferns
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Orchidaceae" title="Orchidaceae">
        orchids
       </a>
       are abundant in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forest" title="Cloud forest">
        cloud forests
       </a>
       of the region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Bird life in the forests of the central region includes
       <a href="/wiki/Resplendent_quetzal" title="Resplendent quetzal">
        resplendent quetzals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_goldfinch" title="Lesser goldfinch">
        goldfinches
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hummingbird" title="Hummingbird">
        hummingbirds
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jay" title="Jay">
        jays
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Emerald_toucanet" title="Emerald toucanet">
        toucanets
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean_lowlands">
        Caribbean lowlands
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Caribbean lowlands">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       This large
       <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">
        rainforest
       </a>
       region is irrigated by several large rivers and is sparsely populated. The area has 57% of the territory of the nation and most of its mineral resources. It has been heavily exploited, but much natural diversity remains. The
       <a href="/wiki/Coco_River" title="Coco River">
        Rio Coco
       </a>
       is the largest river in Central America; it forms the border with Honduras. The Caribbean coastline is much more sinuous than its generally straight Pacific counterpart; lagoons and deltas make it very irregular.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua's
       <a href="/wiki/Bosaw%C3%A1s_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Bosawás Biosphere Reserve">
        Bosawás Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       is in the Atlantic lowlands, part of which is located in the municipality of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siuna" title="Siuna">
        Siuna
       </a>
       ; it protects 7,300 square kilometres (1,800,000 acres) of
       <a href="/wiki/La_Mosquitia" title="La Mosquitia">
        La Mosquitia
       </a>
       forest – almost 7% of the country's area – making it the largest rainforest north of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" title="Amazon Rainforest">
        Amazon
       </a>
       in Brazil.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The municipalities of Siuna,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosita,_Regi%C3%B3n_Aut%C3%B3noma_del_Atl%C3%A1ntico_Norte" title="Rosita, Región Autónoma del Atlántico Norte">
        Rosita
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Bonanza,_North_Caribbean_Coast_Autonomous_Region" title="Bonanza, North Caribbean Coast Autonomous Region">
        Bonanza
       </a>
       , known as the "Mining Triangle", are located in the region known as the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Caribbean_Coast_Autonomous_Region" title="North Caribbean Coast Autonomous Region">
        RAAN
       </a>
       , in the Caribbean lowlands. Bonanza still contains an active gold mine owned by HEMCO. Siuna and Rosita do not have active mines but panning for gold is still very common in the region.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua's tropical east coast is very different from the rest of the country. The climate is predominantly tropical, with high temperature and high humidity. Around the area's principal city of Bluefields, English is widely spoken along with the official Spanish. The population more closely resembles that found in many typical Caribbean ports than the rest of Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A great variety of birds can be observed including
       <a href="/wiki/Eagle" title="Eagle">
        eagles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">
        turkeys
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Toucan" title="Toucan">
        toucans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Parakeet" title="Parakeet">
        parakeets
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Macaw" title="Macaw">
        macaws
       </a>
       . Animal life in the area includes different species of
       <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">
        monkeys
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anteater" title="Anteater">
        anteaters
       </a>
       , white-tailed
       <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">
        deer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tapir" title="Tapir">
        tapirs
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_and_environment">
        Nature and environment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Nature and environment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">
        Flora and fauna
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Nicaragua" title="Wildlife of Nicaragua">
        Wildlife of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1334" data-file-width="1867" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg/220px-Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg/330px-Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg/440px-Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turquoise-browed_Motmot_2495425451.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guardabarranco" title="Guardabarranco">
          Guardabarranco
         </a>
         ("ravine-guard") is Nicaragua's national bird.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is home to a rich variety of plants and animals. Nicaragua is located in the middle of the Americas and this privileged location has enabled the country to serve as host to a great biodiversity. This factor, along with the weather and light altitudinal variations, allows the country to harbor 248 species of amphibians and reptiles, 183 species of mammals, 705 bird species, 640 fish species, and about 5,796 species of plants.
      </p>
      <p>
       The region of great forests is located on the eastern side of the country. Rainforests are found in the
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_San_Juan_Department" title="Río San Juan Department">
        Río San Juan Department
       </a>
       and in the autonomous regions of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Caribbean_Coast_Autonomous_Region" title="North Caribbean Coast Autonomous Region">
        RAAN
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/South_Caribbean_Coast_Autonomous_Region" title="South Caribbean Coast Autonomous Region">
        RAAS
       </a>
       . This biome groups together the greatest biodiversity in the country and is largely protected by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indio_Maiz_Biological_Reserve" title="Indio Maiz Biological Reserve">
        Indio Maiz Biological Reserve
       </a>
       in the south and the
       <a href="/wiki/Bosaw%C3%A1s_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Bosawás Biosphere Reserve">
        Bosawás Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       in the north. The Nicaraguan jungles, which represent about 2.4 million acres, are considered the lungs of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       and comprise the second largest-sized rainforest of the Americas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are currently 78 protected areas in Nicaragua, covering more than 22,000 square kilometres (8,500 sq mi), or about 17% of its landmass. These include
       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_refuge" title="Wildlife refuge">
        wildlife refuges
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">
        nature reserves
       </a>
       that shelter a wide range of
       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">
        ecosystems
       </a>
       . There are more than 1,400 animal species classified thus far in Nicaragua. Some 12,000 species of plants have been
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_classification" title="Biological classification">
        classified
       </a>
       thus far in Nicaragua, with an estimated 5,000 species not yet classified.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Bull_shark" title="Bull shark">
        bull shark
       </a>
       is a species of shark that can survive for an extended period of time in fresh water. It can be found in
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nicaragua" title="Lake Nicaragua">
        Lake Nicaragua
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_River_(Nicaragua)" title="San Juan River (Nicaragua)">
        San Juan River
       </a>
       , where it is often referred to as the "Nicaragua shark".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua has recently banned freshwater fishing of the Nicaragua shark and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sawfish" title="Sawfish">
        sawfish
       </a>
       in response to the declining populations of these animals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">
        Climate change
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate change">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Nicaragua was one of the few countries that did not enter an
       <a href="/wiki/Intended_Nationally_Determined_Contributions" title="Intended Nationally Determined Contributions">
        INDC
       </a>
       at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COP21" title="COP21">
        COP21
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua initially chose not to join the Paris Climate Accord because it felt that "much more action is required" by individual countries on restricting global temperature rise.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_10-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, in October 2017, Nicaragua made the decision to join the agreement.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It ratified this agreement on November 22, 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (September 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">

            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">

         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Nicaragua" title="Politics of Nicaragua">
        Politics of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_18_December_2008-6.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nicaragua" title="President of Nicaragua">
          Nicaraguan President
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ortega" title="Daniel Ortega">
          Daniel Ortega
         </a>
         with then
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_President" title="Russian President">
          Russian President
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">
          Dmitry Medvedev
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">
          Moscow
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
          Russia
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Politics of Nicaragua takes place in a framework of a
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       republic, whereby the
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nicaragua" title="President of Nicaragua">
        President of Nicaragua
       </a>
       is both
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       , and of a
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multi-party system
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
        Executive power
       </a>
       is exercised by the government.
       <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">
        Legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in both the government and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Nicaragua" title="National Assembly of Nicaragua">
        national assembly
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        judiciary
       </a>
       is independent of the executive and the legislature.
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 2007 and 2009, Nicaragua's major political parties discussed the possibility of going from a presidential system to a parliamentary system. Their reason: there would be a clear differentiation between the
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       (prime minister) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       (president). Nevertheless, it was later argued that the true reason behind this proposal was to find a legal way for President Ortega to stay in power after January 2012, when his second and last government period was expected to end. Ortega was reelected to a third term in November 2016.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Nicaragua" title="Foreign relations of Nicaragua">
        Foreign relations of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua pursues an independent foreign policy.
       <a href="/wiki/Territorial_disputes_of_Nicaragua" title="Territorial disputes of Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua is in territorial disputes
       </a>
       with Colombia over the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archipelago_de_San_Andres_y_Providencia" title="Archipelago de San Andres y Providencia">
        Archipelago de San Andres y Providencia
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quita_Sueno_Bank" title="Quita Sueno Bank">
        Quita Sueno Bank
       </a>
       and with Costa Rica over a boundary dispute involving the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_River_(Nicaragua)" title="San Juan River (Nicaragua)">
        San Juan River
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Military">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Nicaragua" title="Military of Nicaragua">
        Military of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg">
         <img alt="Afghan MI-17 and An-26" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1680" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg/220px-Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg/330px-Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg/440px-Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afghan_MI-17_and_AN-26.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/An-26" title="An-26">
          AN-26
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-17" title="Mil Mi-17">
          Mi-17
         </a>
         are used by the
         <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Air_Force" title="Nicaraguan Air Force">
          Nicaraguan Air Force
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Nicaragua" title="Military of Nicaragua">
        armed forces of Nicaragua
       </a>
       consists of various military contingents. Nicaragua has an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Army" title="Nicaraguan Army">
        army
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Navy" title="Nicaraguan Navy">
        navy
       </a>
       and an
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Air_Force" title="Nicaraguan Air Force">
        air force
       </a>
       . There are roughly 14,000 active duty personnel, which is much less compared to the numbers seen during the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">
        Nicaraguan Revolution
       </a>
       . Although the army has had a rough military history, a portion of its forces, which were known as the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_(Nicaragua)" title="National Guard (Nicaragua)">
        national guard
       </a>
       , became integrated with what is now the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Nacional_(Nicaragua)" title="Policía Nacional (Nicaragua)">
        National Police of Nicaragua
       </a>
       . In essence, the police became a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">
         gendarmerie
        </a>
       </i>
       . The National Police of Nicaragua are rarely, if ever, labeled as a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">
         gendarmerie
        </a>
       </i>
       . The other elements and manpower that were not devoted to the national police were sent over to cultivate the new Army of Nicaragua.
      </p>
      <p>
       The age to serve in the armed forces is 17 and
       <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">
        conscription
       </a>
       is not imminent. As of 2006
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the military budget was roughly 0.7% of Nicaragua's expenditures.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">
        Law enforcement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2,photo01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2%2Cphoto01.jpg/220px-600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2%2Cphoto01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2%2Cphoto01.jpg/330px-600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2%2Cphoto01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2%2Cphoto01.jpg/440px-600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2%2Cphoto01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:600x400_1329442889_170212amb-nota2,photo01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_Nicaragua" title="National Police of Nicaragua">
          National Police of Nicaragua
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Police_of_Nicaragua" title="National Police of Nicaragua">
        National Police of Nicaragua
       </a>
       Force (in Spanish: La Policía Nacional Nicaragüense) is the national police of Nicaragua. The force is in charge of regular police functions and, at times, works in conjunction with the Nicaraguan military, making it an indirect and rather subtle version of a gendarmerie.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       However, the Nicaraguan National Police work separately and have a different established set of norms than the nation's military.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is the safest country in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       and one of the safest in Latin America, according to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" title="United Nations Development Program">
        United Nations Development Program
       </a>
       , with a homicide rate of 8.7 per 100,000 inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Nicaragua" title="Departments of Nicaragua">
        Departments of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is a
       <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">
        unitary
       </a>
       republic. For administrative purposes it is divided into 15
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_(administrative_division)" title="Department (administrative division)">
        departments
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        departamentos
       </i>
       ) and two self-governing regions (autonomous communities) based on the Spanish model. The departments are then
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Nicaragua" title="Municipalities of Nicaragua">
        subdivided into 153 municipios
       </a>
       (municipalities). The two autonomous regions are the North Caribbean Coast Autonomous Region and South Caribbean Coast Autonomous Region, often referred to as RACCN and RACCS, respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

             <img alt="Flag of the Department of Estelí" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Flag_of_Esteli.svg/22px-Flag_of_Esteli.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Flag_of_Esteli.svg/33px-Flag_of_Esteli.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Flag_of_Esteli.svg/44px-Flag_of_Esteli.svg.png 2x" width="22"/>
