      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Nicaragua" title="Economy of Nicaragua">
        Economy of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_treemap.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="866" data-file-width="1107" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Nicaragua_treemap.png/220px-Nicaragua_treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Nicaragua_treemap.png/330px-Nicaragua_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Nicaragua_treemap.png/440px-Nicaragua_treemap.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_treemap.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A proportional representation of Nicaragua's exports.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is among the poorest countries in the Americas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its gross domestic product (GDP) in
       <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">
        purchasing power parity
       </a>
       (PPP) in 2008 was estimated at $17.37 billion USD.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Agriculture represents 17% of GDP, the highest percentage in Central America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciagdp_138-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ciagdp-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Remittances account for over 15% of the Nicaraguan GDP. Close to one billion dollars are sent to the country by Nicaraguans living abroad.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The economy grew at a rate of about 4% in 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">
        United Nations Development Programme
       </a>
       , 48% of the population of Nicaragua live below the poverty line,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       79.9% of the population live with less than $2 per day,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to UN figures, 80% of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
        indigenous people
       </a>
       (who make up 5% of the population) live on less than $1 per day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the World Bank, Nicaragua ranked as the 123rd best economy for starting a business.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua's economy is "62.7% free" with high levels of fiscal, government, labor, investment, financial, and trade freedom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It ranks as the 61st
       <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">
        freest economy
       </a>
       , and 14th (of 29) in the Americas.
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 2007, Poland and Nicaragua signed an agreement to write off 30.6 million dollars which was borrowed by the Nicaraguan government in the 1980s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Inflation reduced from 33,500% in 1988 to 9.45% in 2006, and the foreign debt was cut in half.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FruitColors.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/FruitColors.jpg/220px-FruitColors.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/FruitColors.jpg/330px-FruitColors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/FruitColors.jpg/440px-FruitColors.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FruitColors.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
          Coffee
         </a>
         is one of the most important exports of Nicaragua. It is grown in
         <a href="/wiki/Jinotega" title="Jinotega">
          Jinotega
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esteli" title="Esteli">
          Esteli
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Segovia_Department" title="Nueva Segovia Department">
          Nueva Segovia
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matagalpa" title="Matagalpa">
          Matagalpa
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Madriz_Department" title="Madriz Department">
          Madriz
         </a>
         , and exported worldwide through
         <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
          North America
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
          Latin America
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
          Europe
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
          Asia
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
          Australia
         </a>
         . Many coffee companies, like
         <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">
          Nestlé
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">
          Starbucks
         </a>
         , buy Nicaraguan coffee.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is primarily an agricultural country; agriculture constitutes 60% of its total exports which annually yield approximately US $300 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nearly two-thirds of the coffee crop comes from the northern part of the central highlands, in the area north and east of the town of Estelí.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Tobacco, grown in the same northern highlands region as coffee, has become an increasingly important cash crop since the 1990s, with annual exports of leaf and cigars in the neighborhood of $200 million per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . Soil erosion and pollution from the heavy use of pesticides have become serious concerns in the cotton district. Yields and exports have both been declining since 1985.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today most of Nicaragua's bananas are grown in the northwestern part of the country near the port of Corinto; sugarcane is also grown in the same district.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
        Cassava
       </a>
       , a root crop somewhat similar to the potato, is an important food in tropical regions. Cassava is also the main ingredient in tapioca pudding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua's agricultural sector has benefited because of the country's strong ties to
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       . It is estimated that Venezuela will import approximately $200 million in agricultural goods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 1990s, the government initiated efforts to diversify agriculture. Some of the new export-oriented crops were peanuts,
       <a href="/wiki/Sesame" title="Sesame">
        sesame
       </a>
       , melons, and onions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Fishing boats on the Caribbean side bring shrimp as well as lobsters into processing plants at Puerto Cabezas, Bluefields, and Laguna de Perlas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A turtle fishery thrived on the Caribbean coast before it collapsed from
       <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">
        overexploitation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Mining is becoming a major industry in Nicaragua,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       contributing less than 1% of gross domestic product (GDP). Restrictions are being placed on lumbering due to increased environmental concerns about destruction of the rain forests. But lumbering continues despite these obstacles; indeed, a single hardwood tree may be worth thousands of dollars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the war between the US-backed Contras and the government of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">
        Sandinistas
       </a>
       in the 1980s, much of the country's infrastructure was damaged or destroyed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Transportation throughout the nation is often inadequate. For example, one cannot travel all the way by highway from Managua to the Caribbean coast. The road ends at the town of
       <a href="/wiki/El_Rama" title="El Rama">
        El Rama
       </a>
       . Travelers have to transfer and make the rest of the trip by
       <a href="/wiki/Riverboat" title="Riverboat">
        riverboat
       </a>
       down the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Escondido_(Nicaragua)" title="Río Escondido (Nicaragua)">
        Río Escondido
       </a>
       —a five-hour journey.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Centroamérica power plant on the
       <a href="/wiki/Tuma_River" title="Tuma River">
        Tuma River
       </a>
       in the Central highlands has been expanded, and other hydroelectric projects have been undertaken to help provide electricity to the nation's newer industries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua has long been considered as a possible site for a new sea-level canal that could supplement the Panama Canal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua's minimum wage is among the lowest in the Americas and in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
        <a href="#cite_note-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Remittances are equivalent to roughly 15% of the country's gross domestic product.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Growth in the
       <i>
        maquila
       </i>
       sector slowed in the first decade of the 21st century with rising competition from Asian markets, particularly China.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Land is the traditional basis of wealth in Nicaragua, with great fortunes coming from the export of staples such as coffee, cotton, beef, and sugar. Almost all of the upper class and nearly a quarter of the middle class are substantial landowners.
      </p>
      <p>
       A 1985 government study classified 69.4 percent of the population as poor on the basis that they were unable to satisfy one or more of their basic needs in housing, sanitary services (water, sewage, and garbage collection), education, and employment. The defining standards for this study were very low; housing was considered substandard if it was constructed of discarded materials with dirt floors or if it was occupied by more than four persons per room.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rural workers are dependent on agricultural wage labor, especially in coffee and cotton. Only a small fraction hold permanent jobs. Most are migrants who follow crops during the harvest period and find other work during the off-season. The "lower" peasants are typically smallholders without sufficient land to sustain a family; they also join the harvest labor force. The "upper" peasants have sufficient resources to be economically independent. They produce enough surplus, beyond their personal needs, to allow them to participate in the national and world markets.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg/220px-Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg/330px-Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg/440px-Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rotonda_Ruben_dario.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The capital city
         <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">
          Managua
         </a>
         at night
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The urban lower class is characterized by the informal sector of the economy. The informal sector consists of small-scale enterprises that utilize traditional technologies and operate outside the legal regime of labor protections and taxation. Workers in the informal sector are self-employed, unsalaried family workers or employees of small-enterprises, and they are generally poor.
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua's informal sector workers include tinsmiths, mattress makers, seamstresses, bakers, shoemakers, and carpenters; people who take in laundry and ironing or prepare food for sale in the streets; and thousands of peddlers, owners of small businesses (often operating out of their own homes), and market stall operators. Some work alone, but others labor in the small talleres (workshops/factories) that are responsible for a large share of the country's industrial production. Because informal sector earnings are generally very low, few families can subsist on one income.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicaragua_–_SOCIETY_156-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nicaragua_–_SOCIETY-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Like most Latin American nations Nicaragua is also characterized by a very small upper-class, roughly 2% of the population, that is very wealthy and wields the political and economic power in the country that is not in the hands of foreign corporations and private industries. These families are oligarchical in nature and have ruled Nicaragua for generations and their wealth is politically and economically horizontally and vertically integrated.
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is currently a member of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">
        Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas
       </a>
       , which is also known as ALBA. ALBA has proposed creating a new currency, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SUCRE_(currency)" title="SUCRE (currency)">
        Sucre
       </a>
       , for use among its members. In essence, this means that the Nicaraguan córdoba will be replaced with the Sucre. Other nations that will follow a similar pattern include:
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       , Ecuador,
       <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">
        Bolivia
       </a>
       , Honduras,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       , Saint Vincent and the Grenadines,
       <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">
        Dominica
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">
        Antigua and Barbuda
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is considering construction of a canal linking the Atlantic to the Pacific Ocean, which President Daniel Ortega has said will give Nicaragua its "economic independence."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The project was scheduled to begin construction in December 2014,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       however the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua_Canal" title="Nicaragua Canal">
        Nicaragua Canal
       </a>
       has yet to be started.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nicaragua" title="Tourism in Nicaragua">
        Tourism in Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg/220px-Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg/330px-Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg/440px-Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crucero_en_San_Juan.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Royal_Caribbean_International" title="Royal Caribbean International">
          Royal Caribbean
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">
          Cruise ship
         </a>
         docked near the beach at
         <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_del_Sur" title="San Juan del Sur">
          San Juan del Sur
         </a>
         in Southern Nicaragua.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By 2006, tourism had become the second largest industry in Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Previously, tourism had grown about 70% nationwide during a period of 7 years, with rates of 10%–16% annually.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C2_162-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-C2-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The increase and growth led to the income from tourism to rise more than 300% over a period of 10 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The growth in tourism has also positively affected the agricultural, commercial, and finance industries, as well as the construction industry. President
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ortega" title="Daniel Ortega">
        Daniel Ortega
       </a>
       has stated his intention to use tourism to combat poverty throughout the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nica_164-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nica-164">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The results for Nicaragua's tourism-driven economy have been significant, with the nation welcoming one million tourists in a calendar year for the first time in its history in 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="771" data-file-width="1080" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg/220px-HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg/330px-HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg/440px-HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HuellasdeAcahualinca.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ancient_footprints_of_Acahualinca" title="Ancient footprints of Acahualinca">
          2,100-year-old human footprints
         </a>
         called "Huellas de Acahualinca" preserved in volcanic mud near
         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Managua" title="Lake Managua">
          Lake Managua
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Every year about 60,000 U.S. citizens visit Nicaragua, primarily business people, tourists, and those visiting relatives.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some 5,300 people from the U.S. reside in Nicaragua. The majority of tourists who visit Nicaragua are from the U.S., Central or South America, and Europe. According to the Ministry of Tourism of Nicaragua (INTUR),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the colonial cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Nicaragua" title="León, Nicaragua">
        León
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Granada,_Nicaragua" title="Granada, Nicaragua">
        Granada
       </a>
       are the preferred spots for tourists. Also, the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Masaya" title="Masaya">
        Masaya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rivas,_Nicaragua" title="Rivas, Nicaragua">
        Rivas
       </a>
       and the likes of
       <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_del_Sur" title="San Juan del Sur">
        San Juan del Sur
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/El_Ostional" title="El Ostional">
        El Ostional
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_the_Immaculate_Conception" title="Fortress of the Immaculate Conception">
        Fortress of the Immaculate Conception
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ometepe_Island" title="Ometepe Island">
        Ometepe Island
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mombacho" title="Mombacho">
        Mombacho
       </a>
       volcano, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Corn_Islands" title="Corn Islands">
        Corn Islands
       </a>
       among other locations are the main tourist attractions. In addition,
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Recreational_fishing" title="Recreational fishing">
        sport fishing
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">
        surfing
       </a>
       attract many tourists to Nicaragua.
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <i>
        TV Noticias
       </i>
       news program, the main attractions in Nicaragua for tourists are the beaches, the scenic routes, the architecture of cities such as León and Granada,
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Agritourism" title="Agritourism">
        agritourism
       </a>
       particularly in northern Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C2_162-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-C2-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result of increased tourism, Nicaragua has seen its
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">
        foreign direct investment
       </a>
       increase by 79.1% from 2007 to 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua is referred to as
       <i>
        "the land of lakes and volcanoes"
       </i>
       due to the number of lagoons and lakes, and the chain of volcanoes that runs from the north to the south along the country's Pacific side.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brierley_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brierley-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wallace_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wallace-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNTravel_169-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNNTravel-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Today, only 7 of the 50 volcanoes in Nicaragua are considered active. Many of these volcanoes offer some great possibilities for tourists with activities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">
        hiking
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Climbing" title="Climbing">
        climbing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Camping" title="Camping">
        camping
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_swimming" title="Human swimming">
        swimming
       </a>
       in crater lakes.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LagunaApoyo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="789" data-file-width="2048" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/LagunaApoyo.jpg/220px-LagunaApoyo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/LagunaApoyo.jpg/330px-LagunaApoyo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/LagunaApoyo.jpg/440px-LagunaApoyo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LagunaApoyo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Apoyo_Lagoon_Natural_Reserve" title="Apoyo Lagoon Natural Reserve">
          Apoyo Lagoon Natural Reserve
         </a>
         is a nature reserve located between the departments of
         <a href="/wiki/Masaya" title="Masaya">
          Masaya
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
          Granada
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Apoyo_Lagoon_Natural_Reserve" title="Apoyo Lagoon Natural Reserve">
        Apoyo Lagoon Natural Reserve
       </a>
       was created by the eruption of the Apoyo Volcano about 23,000 years ago, which left a huge 7 km-wide crater that gradually filled with water. It is surrounded by the old crater wall.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rim of the lagoon is lined with restaurants, many of which have
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kayaks" title="Kayaks">
        kayaks
       </a>
       available. Besides exploring the forest around it, many water sports are practiced in the lagoon, most notably
       <a href="/wiki/Kayaking" title="Kayaking">
        kayaking
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
        <a href="#cite_note-171">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Sand skiing has become a popular attraction at the
       <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Negro" title="Cerro Negro">
        Cerro Negro
       </a>
       volcano in
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Nicaragua" title="León, Nicaragua">
        León
       </a>
       . Both dormant and active volcanoes can be climbed. Some of the most visited volcanoes include the
       <a href="/wiki/Masaya_Volcano" title="Masaya Volcano">
        Masaya Volcano
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Momotombo" title="Momotombo">
        Momotombo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mombacho" title="Mombacho">
        Mombacho
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cosig%C3%BCina" title="Cosigüina">
        Cosigüina
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ometepe" title="Ometepe">
        Ometepe
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Maderas" title="Maderas">
        Maderas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_(volcano)" title="Concepción (volcano)">
        Concepción
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicaraguasee03.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nicaraguasee03.JPG/220px-Nicaraguasee03.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nicaraguasee03.JPG/330px-Nicaraguasee03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nicaraguasee03.JPG/440px-Nicaraguasee03.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicaraguasee03.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Solentiname_Islands" title="Solentiname Islands">
          Solentiname Islands
         </a>
         are tropical islands located in
         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nicaragua" title="Lake Nicaragua">
          Lake Nicaragua
         </a>
         which are home to 76 bird species and are a growing ecotourism destination.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        Ecotourism
       </a>
       aims to be ecologically and socially conscious; it focuses on local culture, wilderness, and adventure. Nicaragua's ecotourism is growing with every passing year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
        <a href="#cite_note-172">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It boasts a number of ecotourist tours and perfect places for adventurers. Nicaragua has three eco-regions (the Pacific, Central, and Atlantic) which contain volcanoes, tropical rainforests, and agricultural land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
        <a href="#cite_note-173">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The majority of the eco-lodges and other environmentally-focused touristic destinations are found on Ometepe Island,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
        <a href="#cite_note-174">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
       located in the middle of Lake Nicaragua just an hour's boat ride from Granada. While some are foreign-owned, such as the tropical permaculture lodge at
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.ometepezopilote.com/TheFarm.html" rel="nofollow">
        Finca El Zopilote
       </a>
       , others are owned by local families, like the small but well-acclaimed
       <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150813153821/http://fincasverdes.com/inf?tokem=20" rel="nofollow">
        Finca Samaria
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguans" title="Nicaraguans">
        Nicaraguans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Nicaragua" title="Demographics of Nicaragua">
        Demographics of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nica_Women.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="1000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Nica_Women.jpg/220px-Nica_Women.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Nica_Women.jpg/330px-Nica_Women.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Nica_Women.jpg/440px-Nica_Women.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nica_Women.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nicaraguan women at a concert in Managua.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_boys.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="388" data-file-width="500" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Nicaragua_boys.jpg/220px-Nicaragua_boys.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Nicaragua_boys.jpg/330px-Nicaragua_boys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Nicaragua_boys.jpg/440px-Nicaragua_boys.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_boys.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nicaraguan High school students at the
         <a href="/wiki/American_Nicaraguan_School" title="American Nicaraguan School">
          American Nicaraguan School
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to a 2014 research published in the journal
       <i>
        Genetics and Molecular Biology
       </i>
       , European ancestry predominates in 69% of Nicaraguans, followed by African ancestry in 20%, and lastly
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        Native American
       </a>
       ancestry in 11%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
        <a href="#cite_note-175">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A Japanese research of "Genomic Components in America's demography" demonstrated that, on average, the ancestry of Nicaraguans is 58-62% European, 28% Native American, and 14% African, with a very small Near Eastern contribution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
        <a href="#cite_note-176">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Non-genetic data from the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">
         CIA World Factbook
        </a>
       </i>
       establish that from Nicaragua's 2016 population of 5,966,798, around 69% are
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        mestizo
       </a>
       , 17%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" title="White Latin American">
        white
       </a>
       , 5% Native American, and 9%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Latin_American" title="Afro-Latin American">
        black and other races
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This fluctuates with changes in migration patterns. The population is 58% urban as of 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
        <a href="#cite_note-177">
         [177]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The capital
       <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">
        Managua
       </a>
       is the biggest city, with an estimated population of 1,042,641 in 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
        <a href="#cite_note-178">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2005, over 5 million people lived in the Pacific, Central and North regions, and 700,000 in the Caribbean region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CN_179-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CN-179">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a growing expatriate community,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
        <a href="#cite_note-180">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the majority of whom move for business, investment or retirement from across the world, such as from the US,
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">
        Taiwan
       </a>
       , and European countries; the majority have settled in Managua,
       <a href="/wiki/Granada,_Nicaragua" title="Granada, Nicaragua">
        Granada
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_del_Sur" title="San Juan del Sur">
        San Juan del Sur
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Diaspora" title="Nicaraguan Diaspora">
        Nicaraguans live abroad
       </a>
       , particularly in Costa Rica, the United States, Spain, Canada, and other Central American countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
        <a href="#cite_note-181">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua has a population growth rate of 1.5% as of 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is the result of one of the highest
       <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">
        birth rates
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
        Western Hemisphere
       </a>
       : 24.9 per 1,000 according to the United Nations for the period 2005–2010.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The death rate was 4.7 per 1,000 during the same period according to the United Nations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
        <a href="#cite_note-183">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AfroNicoya.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="315" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/AfroNicoya.jpg/170px-AfroNicoya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/AfroNicoya.jpg/255px-AfroNicoya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/AfroNicoya.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AfroNicoya.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An African-Nicaraguan.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The majority of the Nicaraguan population is composed of mestizos, roughly 69%. 17% of Nicaragua's population is of unmixed European stock, with the majority of them being of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
        Spanish
       </a>
       descent, while others are of
       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">
        German
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">
        Italian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">
        English
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">
        Turkish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Danes" title="Danes">
        Danish
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
        French
       </a>
       ancestry.
      </p>
      <p>
       About 9% of Nicaragua's population is black and mainly resides on the country's Caribbean (or Atlantic) coast. The black population is mostly composed of black English-speaking Creoles who are the descendants of escaped or shipwrecked slaves; many carry the name of Scottish settlers who brought slaves with them, such as Campbell, Gordon, Downs and Hodgeson. Although many Creoles supported Somoza because of his close association with the US, they rallied to the Sandinista cause in July 1979 only to reject the revolution soon afterwards in response to a new phase of 'westernization' and imposition of central rule from Managua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
        <a href="#cite_note-184">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is a smaller number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garifuna_people" title="Garifuna people">
        Garifuna
       </a>
       , a people of mixed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_African" title="West African">
        West African
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Island_Carib" title="Island Carib">
        Carib
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">
        Arawak
       </a>
       descent. In the mid-1980s, the government divided the
       <a href="/wiki/Zelaya_Department" title="Zelaya Department">
        Zelaya Department
       </a>
       – consisting of the eastern half of the country – into two autonomous regions and granted the black and indigenous people of this region limited self-rule within the republic.
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="Amerindians">
       </span>
       The remaining 5% of Nicaraguans are Native Americans, the descendants of the country's indigenous inhabitants. Nicaragua's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">
        pre-Columbian
       </a>
       population consisted of many indigenous groups. In the western region, the Nahua (Pipil-Nicarao) people were present along with other groups such as the Chorotega people and the Subtiabas (also known as Maribios or Hokan Xiu). The central region and the Caribbean coast of Nicaragua were inhabited by indigenous peoples who were
       <a href="/wiki/Macro-Chibchan_languages" title="Macro-Chibchan languages">
        Macro-Chibchan language
       </a>
       groups that had migrated to and from South America in ancient times, primarily what is now
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       . These groups include the present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Cacaopera_people" title="Cacaopera people">
        Matagalpas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Miskito_people" title="Miskito people">
        Miskitos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rama_people" title="Rama people">
        Ramas
       </a>
       , as well as Mayangnas and Ulwas who are also known as
       <a href="/wiki/Sumo_people" title="Sumo people">
        Sumos
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brief_22-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-Brief-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         20
        </span>
       </sup>
       In the 19th century, there was a substantial indigenous minority, but this group was largely assimilated culturally into the mestizo majority.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Nicaragua" title="Languages of Nicaragua">
        Languages of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BluefieldsSign.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="737" data-file-width="900" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BluefieldsSign.jpg/220px-BluefieldsSign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BluefieldsSign.jpg/330px-BluefieldsSign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BluefieldsSign.jpg/440px-BluefieldsSign.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BluefieldsSign.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A sign in Bluefields in English (top), Spanish (middle) and Miskito (bottom)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Spanish" title="Nicaraguan Spanish">
        Nicaraguan Spanish
       </a>
       has many indigenous influences and several distinguishing characteristics. For example, some Nicaraguans have a tendency to replace
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant">
        /s/
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">
        /h/
       </a>
       when speaking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
        <a href="#cite_note-185">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although Spanish is spoken throughout, the country has great variety: vocabulary, accents and colloquial language can vary between towns and departments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
        <a href="#cite_note-186">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On the Caribbean coast, indigenous languages,
       <a href="/wiki/English-based_creole_languages" title="English-based creole languages">
        English-based creoles
       </a>
       , and Spanish are spoken. The
       <a href="/wiki/Miskito_language" title="Miskito language">
        Miskito language
       </a>
       , spoken by the
       <a href="/wiki/Miskito_people" title="Miskito people">
        Miskito people
       </a>
       as a first language and some other indigenous and Afro-descendants people as a second, third, or fourth language, is the most commonly spoken indigenous language. The indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Misumalpan_languages" title="Misumalpan languages">
        Misumalpan languages
       </a>
       of Mayangna and Ulwa are spoken by the respective peoples of the same names. Many Miskito, Mayangna, and Ulwa people also speak
       <a href="/wiki/Miskito_Coast_Creole" title="Miskito Coast Creole">
        Miskito Coast Creole
       </a>
       , and a large majority also speak Spanish. Fewer than three dozen of nearly 2,000
       <a href="/wiki/Rama_people" title="Rama people">
        Rama people
       </a>
       speak their
       <a href="/wiki/Chibchan_languages" title="Chibchan languages">
        Chibchan
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Rama_language" title="Rama language">
        language
       </a>
       fluently, with nearly all Ramas speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Rama_Cay_Creole" title="Rama Cay Creole">
        Rama Cay Creole
       </a>
       and the vast majority speaking Spanish. Linguists have attempted to document and revitalize the language over the past three decades.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
        <a href="#cite_note-187">
         [187]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garifuna_people" title="Garifuna people">
        Garifuna people
       </a>
       , descendants of indigenous and Afro-descendant people who came to Nicaragua from Honduras in the early twentieth century, have recently attempted to revitalize their
       <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">
        Arawakan
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Garifuna_language" title="Garifuna language">
        language
       </a>
       . The majority speak Miskito Coast Creole as their first language and Spanish as their second. The Creole or Kriol people, descendants of enslaved Africans brought to the
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       during the British colonial period and European, Chinese, Arab, and British West Indian immigrants, also speak Miskito Coast Creole as their first language and Spanish as their second.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
        <a href="#cite_note-188">
         [188]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">
        Largest cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Largest cities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="navbox">
       <tr>
        <th class="navbox-title" colspan="10">
         <div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">
         </div>
         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="float: left;height:2.6em;">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:Largest_cities_of_Nicaragua" title="Template:Largest cities of Nicaragua">
             <abbr title="View this template">
              v
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-talk">
            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Largest_cities_of_Nicaragua" title="Template talk:Largest cities of Nicaragua">
             <abbr title="Discuss this template">
              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Largest_cities_of_Nicaragua&amp;action=edit">
             <abbr title="Edit this template">
              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
         <div style="height:2.6em;line-height:1.3em;">
          <span style="font-size:110%;">
           Largest
           <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Nicaragua" title="Municipalities of Nicaragua">
            municipalities
           </a>
           in Nicaragua
          </span>
          <br/>
          <span style="font-weight:normal;">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.inide.gob.ni/Anuarios/Anuario%20Estadistico%202015.pdf" rel="nofollow">
            Anuario Estadístico 2015, pp. 50–53
           </a>
           (2016 projections)
          </span>
         </div>
        </th>
       </tr>
