      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Nicaragua" title="Religion in Nicaragua">
        Religion in Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG/290px-Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG/435px-Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG/580px-Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG 2x" width="290"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kathedrale_Leon_2.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_Cathedral_(Nicaragua)" title="León Cathedral (Nicaragua)">
          León Cathedral
         </a>
         , one of Nicaragua's
         <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
          World Heritage Sites
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Religion plays a significant part of the culture of Nicaragua and is afforded special protections in the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Nicaragua" title="Constitution of Nicaragua">
        constitution
       </a>
       . Religious freedom, which has been guaranteed since 1939, and religious tolerance are promoted by the government and the constitution.
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua has no official religion. Catholic bishops are expected to lend their authority to important state occasions, and their pronouncements on national issues are closely followed. They can be called upon to mediate between contending parties at moments of political crisis.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOCR_189-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOCR-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1979, Miguel D'Escoto Brockman, a priest who had embraced
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberation_Theology" title="Liberation Theology">
        Liberation Theology
       </a>
       , served in the government as foreign minister when the Sandinistas came to power. The largest denomination, and traditionally the religion of the majority, is Roman Catholic. Roman Catholicism came to Nicaragua in the 16th century with the Spanish conquest and remained, until 1939, the established faith.
      </p>
      <p>
       The numbers of practising Roman Catholics have been declining, while members of
       <a href="/wiki/Evangelism" title="Evangelism">
        evangelical
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestant
       </a>
       groups and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        Mormons
       </a>
       have been rapidly growing since the 1990s. There are also strong
       <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">
        Anglican
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">
        Moravian
       </a>
       communities on the Caribbean coast in what constituted the sparsely populated
       <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">
        Mosquito Coast
       </a>
       colony, which came under British influence for nearly three centuries. British and German colonists brought
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestantism
       </a>
       , respectively in forms of
       <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">
        Anglicanism
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">
        Moravian Church
       </a>
       . Other kinds of Protestant and other
       <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">
        Christian denominations
       </a>
       were introduced to the rest of Nicaragua during the 19th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       Popular religion revolves around the saints, who are perceived as intercessors (but not mediators) between human beings and God. Most localities, from the capital of Managua to small rural communities, honour
       <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">
        patron saints
       </a>
       , selected from the Roman Catholic calendar, with annual
       <i>
        fiestas
       </i>
       . In many communities, a rich lore has grown up around the celebrations of patron saints, such as Managua's Saint Dominic (Santo Domingo), honoured in August with two colourful, often riotous, day-long processions through the city. The high point of Nicaragua's religious calendar for the masses is neither Christmas nor Easter, but La Purísima, a week of festivities in early December dedicated to the
       <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">
        Immaculate Conception
       </a>
       , during which elaborate altars to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mary_(mother_of_Jesus)" title="Mary (mother of Jesus)">
        Virgin Mary
       </a>
       are constructed in homes and workplaces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOCR_189-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LOCR-189">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a significant
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        LDS
       </a>
       missionary effort in Nicaragua, with two missions, and 95,768 Mormons (1.54% of the population).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The country's close political ties have encouraged religious ties.
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       has increased with a steady influx of immigration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">
        Immigration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Immigration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Relative to its overall population, Nicaragua has never experienced any large-scale immigrant waves. The number of immigrants to Nicaragua, both originating from other Latin American countries and all other countries, never surpassed 1% of its total population before 1995. The 2005 census showed the foreign-born population at 1.2%, having risen a mere .06% in 10 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CN_179-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CN-179">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 19th century, Nicaragua experienced modest waves of immigration from Europe. In particular, families from Germany, Italy, Spain, France and Belgium immigrated to Nicaragua, particularly the departments in the Central and Pacific region.
      </p>
      <p>
       Also present is a small Middle Eastern-Nicaraguan community of
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Syria" title="Demographics of Syria">
        Syrians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">
        Armenians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_of_Nicaragua" title="History of the Jews of Nicaragua">
        Jewish Nicaraguans
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanese
       </a>
       people in Nicaragua with a population of about 30,000. There is an East Asian community mostly consisting of
       <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">
        Chinese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_people" title="Taiwanese people">
        Taiwanese
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_people" title="Japanese people">
        Japanese
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Nicaraguan" title="Chinese Nicaraguan">
        Chinese Nicaraguan
       </a>
       population is estimated at around 12,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
        <a href="#cite_note-192">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Chinese arrived in the late 19th century but were unsubstantiated until the 1920s.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">
        Diaspora
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Diaspora">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_diaspora" title="Nicaraguan diaspora">
        Nicaraguan diaspora
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Civil War forced many Nicaraguans to start lives outside of their country. Many people emigrated during the 1990s and the first decade of the 21st century due to the lack of employment opportunities and poverty. The majority of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Diaspora" title="Nicaraguan Diaspora">
        Nicaraguan Diaspora
       </a>
       migrated to the United States and
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       . Today one in six Nicaraguans live in these two countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
        <a href="#cite_note-193">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The diaspora has seen Nicaraguans settling around in smaller communities in other parts of the world, particularly Western Europe. Small communities of Nicaraguans are found in France, Germany, Italy, Spain, Norway, Sweden and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       . Communities also exist in Australia and New Zealand. Canada, Brazil and Argentina host small groups of these communities. In Asia, Japan hosts a small Nicaraguan community.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to extreme poverty at home, many Nicaraguans are now living and working in neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       , a country that has the US dollar as currency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
        <a href="#cite_note-194">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
        <a href="#cite_note-195">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">
        Healthcare
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Healthcare">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Nicaragua" title="Healthcare in Nicaragua">
        Healthcare in Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although Nicaragua's health outcomes have improved over the past few decades with the efficient utilization of resources relative to other Central American nations,
       <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Nicaragua" title="Healthcare in Nicaragua">
        healthcare in Nicaragua
       </a>
       still confronts challenges responding to its populations' diverse healthcare needs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_196-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-196">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Nicaragua" title="Government of Nicaragua">
        Nicaraguan government
       </a>
       guarantees universal free
       <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">
        health care
       </a>
       for its citizens.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_197-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-197">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, limitations of current delivery models and unequal distribution of resources and medical personnel contribute to the persistent lack of quality care in more remote areas of Nicaragua, especially amongst rural communities in the Central and Atlantic region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_196-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-196">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To respond to the dynamic needs of localities, the government has adopted a decentralized model that emphasizes community-based preventative and primary medical care.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
        <a href="#cite_note-198">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Nicaragua" title="Education in Nicaragua">
        Education in Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edificio_UNI.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="285" data-file-width="583" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Edificio_UNI.jpg/220px-Edificio_UNI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Edificio_UNI.jpg/330px-Edificio_UNI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Edificio_UNI.jpg/440px-Edificio_UNI.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edificio_UNI.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Universidad Nacional De Ingeniería "National University of Engineering",
         <a href="/wiki/Managua" title="Managua">
          Managua
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The adult literacy rate in 2005 was 78.0%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescolit_199-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unescolit-199">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Primary education is free in Nicaragua. A system of private schools exists, many of which are religiously affiliated and often have more robust English programs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
        <a href="#cite_note-200">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 1979, the educational system was one of the poorest in Latin America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NE_201-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NE-201">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the first acts of the newly elected Sandinista government in 1980 was an extensive and successful literacy campaign, using secondary school students, university students and teachers as volunteer teachers: it reduced the overall illiteracy rate from 50.3% to 12.9% within only five months.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NLC_202-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NLC-202">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was one of a number of large-scale programs which received international recognition for their gains in
       <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">
        literacy
       </a>
       , health care, education,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Childcare" title="Childcare">
        childcare
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">
        unions
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">
        land reform
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
        <a href="#cite_note-204">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Sandinistas also added a leftist ideological content to the curriculum, which was removed after 1990.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 1980,
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       awarded Nicaragua the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       sponsored
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Nadezhda_K._Krupskaya_literacy_prize" title="UNESCO Nadezhda K. Krupskaya literacy prize">
        Nadezhda Krupskaya award
       </a>
       for the literacy campaign.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [205]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The majority of higher education institutions are in Managua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
        <a href="#cite_note-206">
         [206]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua's higher education system consists of 48 universities, and 113 colleges and technical institutes in the areas of
       <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">
        electronics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">
        computer systems
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">
        sciences
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Agroforestry" title="Agroforestry">
        agroforestry
       </a>
       , construction and trade-related services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
        <a href="#cite_note-207">
         [207]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2005, almost 400,000 (7%) of Nicaraguans held a
       <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">
        university degree
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
        <a href="#cite_note-208">
         [208]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nicaragua also has several more specialized institutions, with a focus on education that will promote economic development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr1_113-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-gr1-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Nicaragua" title="Culture of Nicaragua">
        Culture of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="616" data-file-width="820" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg/220px-El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg/330px-El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg/440px-El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense" title="El Güegüense">
          El Güegüense
         </a>
         is a
         <a href="/wiki/Drama" title="Drama">
          drama
         </a>
         and was the first literary work of post-Columbian Nicaragua. It is regarded as one of
         <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
          Latin America
         </a>
         's most distinctive colonial-era expressions and as Nicaragua's signature folkloric masterpiece combining music, dance and theatre.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Nicaragua" title="Culture of Nicaragua">
        Nicaraguan culture
       </a>
       has strong folklore, music and religious traditions, deeply influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">
        European culture
       </a>
       but also including Native American sounds and flavors. Nicaraguan culture can further be defined in several distinct strands. The Pacific coast has strong folklore, music and religious traditions, deeply influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Europeans
       </a>
       . It was colonized by Spain and has a similar culture to other Spanish-speaking Latin American countries. The indigenous groups that historically inhabited the Pacific coast have largely been assimilated into the
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        mestizo
       </a>
       culture.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Caribbean coast of Nicaragua was once a British protectorate. English is still predominant in this region and spoken domestically along with Spanish and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Nicaragua" title="Languages of Nicaragua">
        indigenous languages
       </a>
       . Its culture is similar to that of Caribbean nations that were or are British possessions, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
        Jamaica
       </a>
       , Belize, the
       <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
        Cayman Islands
       </a>
       , etc. Unlike on the west coast, the indigenous peoples of the Caribbean coast have maintained distinct identities, and some still speak their native languages as first languages.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nicaragua" title="Music of Nicaragua">
        Music of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nicaragua" title="Music of Nicaragua">
        Nicaraguan music
       </a>
       is a mixture of indigenous and Spanish influences. Musical instruments include the
       <a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">
        marimba
       </a>
       and others common across Central America. The marimba of Nicaragua is played by a sitting performer holding the instrument on his knees. He is usually accompanied by a bass
       <a href="/wiki/Fiddle" title="Fiddle">
        fiddle
       </a>
       , guitar and guitarrilla (a small guitar like a
       <a href="/wiki/Mandolin" title="Mandolin">
        mandolin
       </a>
       ). This music is played at social functions as a sort of background music.
      </p>
      <p>
       The marimba is made with hardwood plates placed over bamboo or metal tubes of varying lengths. It is played with two or four
       <a href="/wiki/Hammer" title="Hammer">
        hammers
       </a>
       . The Caribbean coast of Nicaragua is known for a lively, sensual form of
       <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">
        dance music
       </a>
       called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Palo_de_Mayo" title="Palo de Mayo">
         Palo de Mayo
        </a>
       </i>
       which is popular throughout the country. It is especially loud and celebrated during the Palo de Mayo festival in May. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garifuna_people" title="Garifuna people">
        Garifuna
       </a>
       community (Afro-Native American) is known for its popular music called
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punta_(music)" title="Punta (music)">
         Punta
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1087" data-file-width="600" height="399" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg/220px-Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg/330px-Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg/440px-Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicaragua_Mestizaje.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nicaraguan women wearing the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mestizaje" title="Mestizaje">
          Mestizaje
         </a>
         costume, which is a traditional costume worn to dance the Mestizaje dance. The costume demonstrates the Spanish influence upon Nicaraguan clothing.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209">
          <a href="#cite_note-209">
           [209]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaragua enjoys a variety of international influence in the music arena.
       <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">
        Bachata
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">
        Merengue
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">
        Salsa
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cumbia_music" title="Cumbia music">
        Cumbia
       </a>
       have gained prominence in cultural centres such as Managua, Leon and
       <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
        Granada
       </a>
       . Cumbia dancing has grown popular with the introduction of Nicaraguan artists, including Gustavo Leyton, on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ometepe_Island" title="Ometepe Island">
        Ometepe Island
       </a>
       and in Managua.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salsa_dancing" title="Salsa dancing">
        Salsa dancing
       </a>
       has become extremely popular in Managua's nightclubs. With various influences, the form of salsa dancing varies in Nicaragua. New York style and Cuban Salsa (Salsa Casino) elements have gained popularity across the country.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">
        Dance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Dance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Nicaragua" title="Dance in Nicaragua">
        Dance in Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dance in Nicaragua varies depending upon the region. Rural areas tend to have a stronger focus on movement of the hips and turns. The dance style in cities focuses primarily on more sophisticated footwork in addition to movement and turns. Combinations of styles from the
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
        Dominican Republic
       </a>
       and the United States can be found throughout Nicaragua.
       <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(dance)" title="Bachata (dance)">
        Bachata dancing
       </a>
       is popular in Nicaragua. A considerable amount of Bachata dancing influence comes from Nicaraguans living abroad, in cities that include Miami, Los Angeles and, to a much lesser extent, New York City.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tango_(dance)" title="Tango (dance)">
        Tango
       </a>
       has also surfaced recently in cultural cities and ballroom dance occasions.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literature_of_Nicaragua" title="Literature of Nicaragua">
        Literature of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="291" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg/170px-Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg/255px-Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo" title="Rubén Darío">
          Rubén Darío
         </a>
         , the founder of the
         <a href="/wiki/Modernismo" title="Modernismo">
          modernismo
         </a>
         literary movement in Latin America.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The origin of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Literature_of_Nicaragua" title="Literature of Nicaragua">
        Nicaraguan literature
       </a>
       can arguably be traced to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian" title="Pre-Columbian">
        pre-Columbian
       </a>
       times. The myths and
       <a href="/wiki/Oral_literature" title="Oral literature">
        oral literature
       </a>
       formed the cosmogenic view of the world of the indigenous people. Some of these stories are still known in Nicaragua. Like many Latin American countries, the Spanish conquerors have had the most effect on both the culture and the literature. Nicaraguan literature has historically been an important source of poetry in the Spanish-speaking world, with internationally renowned contributors such as
       <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo" title="Rubén Darío">
        Rubén Darío
       </a>
       who is regarded as the most important literary figure in Nicaragua. He is called the "Father of Modernism" for leading the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Modernismo" title="Modernismo">
         modernismo
        </a>
       </i>
       literary movement at the end of the 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI_210-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NI-210">
         [210]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other literary figures include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Martinez_Rivas" title="Carlos Martinez Rivas">
        Carlos Martinez Rivas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Antonio_Cuadra" title="Pablo Antonio Cuadra">
        Pablo Antonio Cuadra
       </a>
       , Alberto Cuadra Mejia, Manolo Cuadra, Pablo Alberto Cuadra Arguello, Orlando Cuadra Downing, Alfredo Alegría Rosales,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergio_Ramirez_Mercado" title="Sergio Ramirez Mercado">
        Sergio Ramirez Mercado
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Cardenal" title="Ernesto Cardenal">
        Ernesto Cardenal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gioconda_Belli" title="Gioconda Belli">
        Gioconda Belli
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Claribel_Alegr%C3%ADa" title="Claribel Alegría">
        Claribel Alegría
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Coronel_Urtecho" title="José Coronel Urtecho">
        José Coronel Urtecho
       </a>
       , among others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
        <a href="#cite_note-211">
         [211]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The satirical drama
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/El_G%C3%BCeg%C3%BCense" title="El Güegüense">
         El Güegüense
        </a>
       </i>
       was the first literary work of post-Columbian Nicaragua. Written in both Aztec
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       and Spanish it is regarded as one of Latin America's most distinctive colonial-era expressions and as Nicaragua's signature folkloric masterpiece, a work of resistance to Spanish colonialism that combined music, dance and theatre.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NI_210-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NI-210">
         [210]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">
        theatrical
       </a>
       play was written by an anonymous author in the 16th century, making it one of the oldest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_culture" title="Indigenous culture">
        indigenous
       </a>
       theatrical/dance works of the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
        Western Hemisphere
       </a>
       . In 2005 it was recognized by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       as "a patrimony of humanity,"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
        <a href="#cite_note-212">
         [212]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After centuries of popular performance, the play was first published in a book in 1942.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
        <a href="#cite_note-213">
         [213]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_cuisine" title="Nicaraguan cuisine">
        Nicaraguan cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VIGORON.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/VIGORON.JPG/220px-VIGORON.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/VIGORON.JPG/330px-VIGORON.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/VIGORON.JPG/440px-VIGORON.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VIGORON.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Vigor%C3%B3n" title="Vigorón">
          Vigorón
         </a>
         is a dish that is served with vegetables and chicharrones (fried pork with skin or with meat) and wrapped in Banana leaf.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nicaraguan cuisine is a mixture of Spanish food and dishes of a pre-Columbian origin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NICA_214-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NICA-214">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Traditional cuisine changes from the Pacific to the Caribbean coast. The Pacific coast's main staple revolves around local fruits and corn, the Caribbean coast cuisine makes use of seafood and the coconut.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg/220px-Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg/330px-Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg/440px-Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Costa_Rican_Gallo_Pinto.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo_Pinto" title="Gallo Pinto">
          Gallo Pinto
         </a>
         is a traditional dish of Nicaragua made with rice and beans.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As in many other Latin American countries,
       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">
        maize
       </a>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">
        staple food
       </a>
       and is used in many of the widely consumed dishes, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Nacatamal" title="Nacatamal">
        nacatamal
       </a>
       , and
       <i>
        indio viejo
       </i>
       . Maize is also an ingredient for drinks such as
       <a href="/wiki/Pinolillo" title="Pinolillo">
        pinolillo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicha" title="Chicha">
        chicha
       </a>
       as well as sweets and desserts. In addition to corn, rice and beans are eaten very often.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo_pinto" title="Gallo pinto">
        Gallo pinto
       </a>
       , Nicaragua's
       <a href="/wiki/National_dish" title="National dish">
        national dish
       </a>
       , is made with white rice and red beans that are cooked individually and then fried together. The dish has several variations including the addition of
       <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">
        coconut milk
       </a>
       and/or grated
       <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">
        coconut
       </a>
       on the Caribbean coast. Most Nicaraguans begin their day with Gallopinto. Gallopinto is most usually served with
       <i>
        carne asada
       </i>
       , a salad, fried cheese,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooking_bananas" title="Cooking bananas">
        plantains
       </a>
       or maduros.
      </p>
      <p>
       Many of Nicaragua's dishes include indigenous fruits and vegetables such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jocote" title="Jocote">
        jocote
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">
        mango
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">
        papaya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">
        tamarindo
       </a>
       , pipian, banana,
       <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">
        avocado
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">
        yuca
       </a>
       , and herbs such as
       <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">
        cilantro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oregano" title="Oregano">
        oregano
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bixa_orellana" title="Bixa orellana">
        achiote
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NICA_214-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NICA-214">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaraguans have been known to eat
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea_pig" title="Guinea pig">
        guinea pigs
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
        <a href="#cite_note-215">
         [215]
        </a>
       </sup>
       known as
       <i>
        cuy
       </i>
       . Tapirs, iguanas, turtle eggs, armadillos and boas are also sometimes eaten, but because of extinction threats to these wild creatures, there are efforts to curb this custom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NICA_214-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-NICA-214">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Nicaragua" title="Media of Nicaragua">
        Media of Nicaragua
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       For most Nicaraguans radio and TV are the main sources of news. There are more than 100 radio stations and several TV networks. Cable TV is available in most urban areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
        <a href="#cite_note-216">
         [216]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Nicaraguan print media are varied and partisan, representing pro and anti-government positions. Publications include
       <a href="/wiki/La_Prensa_(Managua)" title="La Prensa (Managua)">
        La Prensa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Diario" title="El Nuevo Diario">
        El Nuevo Diario
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Confidencial" title="Confidencial">
        Confidencial
       </a>
       , Hoy, and Mercurio. Online news publications include Confidencial and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Nicaragua_Dispatch" title="The Nicaragua Dispatch">
        The Nicaragua Dispatch
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicaragua&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2518" data-file-width="3777" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg/220px-National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg/330px-National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg/440px-National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_baseball_stadium_Managua.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dennis_Martinez_National_Stadium" title="Dennis Martinez National Stadium">
          Dennis Martinez National Stadium
         </a>
         is Nicaragua's main stadium.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">
        Baseball
       </a>
       is the most popular sport in Nicaragua. Although some professional Nicaraguan baseball teams have recently folded, the country still enjoys a strong tradition of American-style baseball.
      </p>
      <p>
       Baseball was introduced to Nicaragua during the 19th century. In the Caribbean coast, locals from Bluefields were taught how to play baseball in 1888 by Albert Addlesberg, a retailer from the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BB_217-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BB-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Baseball did not catch on in the Pacific coast until 1891 when a group of mostly college students from the United States formed "La Sociedad de Recreo" (Society of Recreation) where they played various sports, baseball being the most popular.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BB_217-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-BB-217">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nicaragua has had its share of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        MLB
       </a>
       players, including short stop
       <a href="/wiki/Everth_Cabrera" title="Everth Cabrera">
        Everth Cabrera
       </a>
       and pitcher
       <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Padilla" title="Vicente Padilla">
        Vicente Padilla
       </a>
       , but the most notable is
       <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Dennis Martínez">
        Dennis Martínez
       </a>
       , who was the first baseball player from Nicaragua to play in
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
        <a href="#cite_note-218">
         [218]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He became the first Latin-born pitcher to throw a
       <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">
        perfect game
       </a>
       , and the 13th in the major league history, when he played with the Montreal Expos against the
       <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">
        Dodgers
       </a>
       at Dodger Stadium in 1991.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
        <a href="#cite_note-219">
         [219]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">
        Boxing
       </a>
       is the second most popular sport in Nicaragua.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
        <a href="#cite_note-220">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country has had world champions such as
       <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Arg%C3%BCello" title="Alexis Argüello">
        Alexis Argüello
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Mayorga" title="Ricardo Mayorga">
        Ricardo Mayorga
       </a>
       as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A1n_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(boxer)" title="Román González (boxer)">
        Román González
       </a>
       . Recently,
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        football
       </a>
       has gained popularity. The
       <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez_National_Stadium" title="Dennis Martínez National Stadium">
        Dennis Martínez National Stadium
       </a>
       has served as a venue for both baseball and football. The first ever national football-only stadium in Managua, the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua_National_Football_Stadium" title="Nicaragua National Football Stadium">
        Nicaragua National Football Stadium
       </a>
       , was completed in 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
        <a href="#cite_note-221">
         [221]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        <li id="cite_note-121">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-121">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <i>
           Alternative Histories of English
          </i>
          edited by Peter Trudgill, Professor of Sociolinguistics and Richard J. Watts. Routledge, 2002. pp 35: "English-speaking protestants formed the majority of the population until about 1900...indigenous anglophones still form about 85 per cent of the population, which also includes non-anglophone Black Caribs...At least at the level of arolectal Whites, the accent is rhotic though obviously Caribbean....England established a protectorate over the local Miskito Indians, who the region is named after, and the area was a British dependency from 1740 to 1786. In Nicaragua the British founded the principal Miskito coast city of Bluefields... There are about 30,000 native speakers of English in this area of Nicaragua who look to Bluefields as their centre... The English of the anglophone Corn Islands is also typically Caribbean."
         </span>
